# IAMS Development Log

Dated, append-only log of what actually got built, day by day. Each entry lists what shipped (with file evidence), what's still partial, and what's next — so "status" is always answerable from this file plus a `git log` rather than from memory.

Story status (Built / Partial / Not started) is tracked per-epic here against `July 10 Updates/files/IAMS_Epics_and_User_Stories_v1.0.md` (180 stories, 17 epics). See that document for the story definitions; this log only tracks build status and dates.

---

## 2026-07-12

**Epic worked:** EPIC-USR — User Management & RBAC (9 stories, 0/9 built at start of day)

**Why this epic first:** per the status review earlier today, EPIC-AST was the only epic with real progress (13/16). Everything else — including finishing AST's remaining stories — either assumes real users/roles exist or is lower-leverage until they do. The existing auth code already had the seam prepared for this: `CurrentUserProvider`, `JwtService`, and `AuthController` all carry comments to the effect of "this is the seam EPIC-USR/SEC replaces, not the contract other code depends on."

**Built today:**
- **US-USR-01** (provision a user with role + org scope) — real, DB-backed. `role_definition` (V15), `app_user` (V16), `user_role_assignment` (V17) migrations; `Role`/`AppUser`/`UserRoleAssignment` domain + repositories; `UserProvisioningService` with the exception AC enforced (only a Super Administrator may assign a `is_sensitive` role); `POST /api/v1/users`.
- **US-USR-07** (flat, non-inheriting roles) — satisfied by construction: `user_role_assignment` is a plain join, one row per role, each role's own `permissions` apply verbatim, nothing unioned or implied beyond a flat union at read time.
- **US-USR-08** (block offboarding while assets remain assigned) — `UserDeactivationService` blocks deactivation via `AssetRepository.findByAssignedToPersonId`, listing the blocking asset numbers; `POST /api/v1/users/{id}/deactivate`. Session/refresh-token revocation named in the same AC is **not** implemented — there's no session store yet (noted in code, not silently skipped).
- Replaced the `DevSecurityProperties.DevUser` hardcoded single-user login stub in `AuthController` with a real lookup against `app_user` — this was the seam the existing code's own comments said EPIC-USR/SEC would replace.
- Added `GET /api/v1/auth/me` (US-USR-01 AC: "shows role, scope, and computed permissions") — wasn't implemented before today.
- `BootstrapUserSeeder`: creates the first Super Administrator at startup from the same `iams.security.dev-user.*` config keys the old stub used (no env var changes needed), hashing the password with the real `PasswordEncoder` bean instead of a hand-computed hash pasted into SQL.

**Bug found and fixed in existing code as a side effect:** every `@PreAuthorize` check across 7 existing controllers (13 checks total, in `asset` and `org`) already hardcoded `hasAnyRole('ADMIN','SUPER_ADMIN')` — written before any real role existed. Seeding the Administrator role as `'ADMINISTRATOR'` (the more obvious choice) would have made all 13 checks silently match nothing. Seeded as `'ADMIN'` instead, matching the existing convention.

**Built later the same day (continuing per "those two are what the rest of RBAC depends on"):**
- **US-USR-04** (org-scope restricts every list/search/detail fetch, partial) — `UserScopeResolver` resolves the acting user's scope fresh from the DB on every call (deliberately not cached in the JWT, since US-USR-04-X requires a narrowed scope to apply on the user's *next* request, not at next login). Wired into `AssetQueryService` (list + get) and `PersonService` (list + get), both previously unscoped; `AssetRepositoryCustomImpl.search` now takes a `scopeOrgNodeId` predicate. Out-of-scope direct-by-id fetches now throw `AccessDeniedException` (403) and log a WARN (AC-USR-04-X) — there's no persistent Security & Access Log yet to write the denial to (that's US-SEC-04/11), so the application log is the interim record, noted as such in code.
  - **Known limitation, not silently papered over:** only exact-org-node matching is possible — `OrgNode` still has no parent/child column (EPIC-ORG hasn't built the hierarchy), so "scope + descendants" (the FR's literal wording) isn't achievable yet. Revisit this once EPIC-ORG lands the hierarchy.
- **US-USR-02** (custom roles with a configurable permission set) — `RoleService`/`RoleController`: `POST/PATCH/DELETE /api/v1/roles` (Super Admin only), `GET` (Admin+). System roles (`is_system=true`) can't be edited or deleted through this API even if someone forgets the controller annotation — the service itself guards it. Delete is blocked with the affected-username list when the role is still assigned to ≥1 user (mirrors the existing `ConflictException`/dependent-list pattern used by `AssetCategoryService`).
- 19 new unit tests (`AssetQueryServiceTest` — new file, this service had zero coverage before today; `RoleServiceTest`; 3 new cases in `PersonServiceTest`), all passing. Full suite: **62/62 passing, no regressions.** `mvn clean test` clean.

**Partial / in progress:**
- US-USR-04: exact-node scope only, no descendants (see above) — blocked on EPIC-ORG.
- Password policy (US-SEC-05) isn't built — `UserProvisioningService` only enforces a minimum length (8 chars) as a guardrail, not a stand-in for the real policy.
- Permission denials are logged via SLF4J, not a queryable Security & Access Log (US-SEC-04/11 don't exist yet).

**Not started (still, within EPIC-USR):**
- US-USR-03 (permission checks enforced at API *and UI*) — only role-based `@PreAuthorize` exists (role, not fine-grained permission-string, checks); nothing on the frontend reads `/auth/me`'s `permissions` to hide controls yet.
- US-USR-05 (System Operator scoped to technical config only) — role is seeded with placeholder permissions but nothing enforces the restriction yet.
- US-USR-06 (block self-approval) — no approval workflow exists yet to self-approve against (depends on LIF/AUD).
- US-USR-09 (SoD waivers) — not started.

**EPIC-USR now stands at:** 3 of 9 stories fully built (US-USR-01, US-USR-02, US-USR-07), 2 partial (US-USR-04, US-USR-08's session-revocation gap), 4 not started (US-USR-03, 05, 06, 09).

**Review pass, same day:** ran a full 7-angle code review (correctness line-scan, removed-behavior audit, cross-file tracer, reuse, simplification, efficiency, altitude) against everything built today, then fixed every confirmed finding:
- **Real crash bug**, not caught by any Mockito test: `AppUser.orgScopeNode` is lazy and `open-in-view` is disabled, so `UserMapper` reading `.getName()` on it *after* `UserQueryService`'s transaction closed threw `LazyInitializationException` on `POST /users` and `GET /users/{id}` for any org-scoped user. Fixed with `JOIN FETCH` query variants in `AppUserRepository`; this class of bug is structurally invisible to mock-based unit tests, which is exactly how it got past this morning's test suite.
- **Security regression**: the new DB-backed login had a timing side-channel — unknown usernames failed fast, known usernames with wrong passwords paid the full BCrypt cost — undermining the exact "never leaks whether a username exists" guarantee its own comment claimed. Fixed: always run the password check (against a dummy hash for unknown usernames), same latency either way.
- **Scope-enforcement gap this session introduced by omission**: `GET /assets/{id}/children` had zero org-scope check (`AssetHierarchyService.listChildren` still used plain `existsById`) — a scoped user blocked from viewing an out-of-scope asset directly could still see its children. Extracted the org-scope check (previously copy-pasted between `AssetQueryService`/`PersonService`) into a shared `OrgScopeGuard`, then wired it into all three services — closing both the gap and the duplication in one move.
- **Scope-bypass bug**: `PersonService.update()` checked scope against a person's *current* org node but never against a *new* one being written, so a scoped actor could relocate a person into a node outside their own authority. Fixed: the new node is now checked too.
- API-spec-compliance gap I found independently while fixing the above: `UserDeactivationService`'s blocked-response used an invented errorCode (`USER_HAS_ASSIGNED_ASSETS`) and a flat message string, when `IAMS_API_Specification_v1.1.md` §4.5 documents an exact contract (`USER_HAS_OUTSTANDING_ASSIGNMENTS`, structured `blockingAssets`/`resolutionActions`). `ConflictException` extended with an optional title + extra-properties payload (backward compatible with its existing simple 2-arg usages elsewhere); fixed to match the ratified spec exactly.
- **N+1 query**: `UserQueryService.list()` issued one role-assignment query per user (plus a further lazy `Role` load per distinct role). Fixed with a single batched `findByUserIdIn` query.
- **Wrong exception semantics**: `RoleService.rejectIfSystem` threw a 400 `ValidationFailedException` pointing at a `code` field `RoleUpdateRequest` doesn't have, for what's actually a 409 state conflict — the sibling check two lines later already used `ConflictException` for the identical class of problem. Fixed to match.
- Also generalized `ApiExceptionHandler`'s conflict handler to derive the `type` URI slug from `errorCode` instead of a single hardcoded `"conflict"` slug for every scenario — a small, low-risk fix that also corrects the pre-existing `AssetCategoryService`/`AssetHierarchyService` conflict responses toward spec compliance, not just today's new code.
- 3 new tests added alongside the fixes (out-of-scope-relocation block, out-of-scope-parent blocks children, out-of-scope-parent-with-in-scope/out-of-scope children filtering). **Full suite: 65/65 passing.**

**Deliberately deferred** (flagged by the review, real but lower priority — not fixed today): no compile-time link between `@PreAuthorize` role-string literals and `role_definition.code` (a future typo like `hasRole('SUPERADMIN')` would silently grant nobody access); no way to revoke a single role from a user without full deactivation (`UserRoleAssignmentRepository.deleteByUserIdAndRoleId` exists but nothing calls it — a real US-USR-07 gap); `AppUserRepository.findByPersonId` is unused (Person offboarding doesn't cascade to deactivate the linked login, if that's even meant to happen); the optimistic-lock retry block and the `BootstrapUserSeeder`/`UserProvisioningService.assignRoles` construction logic are each duplicated 2-3x across services rather than sharing a helper (same root cause the `OrgScopeGuard` extraction just fixed for the scope-check case, not yet done for these).

**Frontend, same day:** built the first UI for EPIC-USR (previously 0 pages across the whole epic).
- `UserListPage` (`/users`): list with status/role chips and org-scope name, "+ New User" dialog (username/password/displayName/email/multi-select roles sourced from the live role catalog), and a deactivate flow that surfaces the backend's structured `blockingAssets`/`resolutionActions` payload (from this morning's API-spec-compliance fix) directly in the confirmation dialog rather than a generic error string.
- `RoleListPage` (`/roles`): list with system/sensitive/non-human badges and permission chips; create/edit/delete gated to Super Administrator in the UI (matching the backend's `@PreAuthorize`), system roles never show edit/delete controls.
- New `api/users/userApi.ts`, `api/roles/roleApi.ts`, `features/users/`, `features/roles/` (types + React Query hooks), following the exact conventions already established by the assets/persons features (query key prefixing, `ApiProblem`-based error handling, dialog-based CRUD).
- `ApiProblem` (frontend `errors.ts`) extended with `blockingAssets`/`resolutionActions` to match the backend contract.
- Nav: added "Users"/"Roles" to `AdminShell`, visible only to ADMIN/SUPER_ADMIN roles (read from the JWT's `roles` claim) — a convenience, not the control; the backend's `@PreAuthorize` is what actually enforces it.
- Cleaned up copy/comments in `authStore.ts`, `decodeJwt.ts`, `LoginPage.tsx` that still said "dev-stub backend" / "single administrator account" — stale since this morning's real-auth work; also dropped the hardcoded `admin` default in the login username field.
- Deliberately **not** built: Person and OrgNode pickers on the user-create form (`personId`, `orgScopeNodeId`) — neither has a list UI yet (EPIC-ORG isn't built beyond the minimal backend CRUD `AssetAssignmentService` needs), so a fake dropdown would be worse than omitting the fields. Both remain settable via direct API call.

**Verification — partial, and here's exactly where it stopped:** `tsc -b` (typecheck) and `oxlint` both clean. Started the Vite dev server and confirmed the app shell and every new/changed module (`UserListPage`, `RoleListPage`, `AdminShell`, `router`, `LoginPage`) transforms and serves without error. **Could not go further than that**: no browser-automation/screenshot tool is available in this environment, so no actual click-through happened, and the backend couldn't be started against a live database — the local Postgres instance has an `iams_app` role, but its password doesn't match `.env.example`'s documented dev default (`iams_dev_password`); rather than guess at credentials for a database I don't know the provenance of, I stopped there. **This means the create-user, create-role, and deactivate-user flows have not actually been exercised end-to-end** - only proven to compile, lint, and transform cleanly. Needs either the real local Postgres credentials or a docker-compose setup (still doesn't exist for this project) before that gap closes.

**Next session:** With a frontend now in place, either (a) get the local Postgres credentials sorted (or stand up docker-compose, which doesn't exist yet for this project) so the flows built today can actually be click-tested, or (b) keep going backend-only into US-USR-03 (permission-based, not just role-based, enforcement) since `role.permissions` and `/auth/me`'s computed `permissions` set already exist and are unused by any `@PreAuthorize` check so far. EPIC-USR migrations remain unvalidated against a live database either way.

---

## 2026-07-13

**Picked up exactly where yesterday stopped:** yesterday's blocker was "no docker-compose, and the local Postgres's password doesn't match the documented dev default, so nothing got click-tested." Added `docker-compose.yml` (Postgres 16 + MinIO, matching `.env.example`'s existing conventions) to fix that for good — except it turned out unnecessary today: a native Postgres was already running on this machine on port 5432 with the exact `iams_app`/`iams_dev_password` credentials `.env.example` documents, already migrated to V17. (Torn the Docker container back down once this was confirmed, so it doesn't fight the native instance for the port; `docker-compose.yml` stays in the repo for machines that don't have a native Postgres.) Booted the real Spring Boot app against it (port 8081, since something unrelated already holds 8080) for the first time this project has actually been click-tested against a live database.

**Three real bugs found in ~10 minutes of click-testing that 68 passing unit tests never caught, all fixed:**
- **`ApiExceptionHandler.handleGeneric` logged nothing.** Every unhandled 500 returned only a traceId with no server-side stack trace to look up — first login attempt returned a 500 and there was nothing in the log to explain why. Added `log.error(...)` with the exception. This is what made the next two bugs findable at all.
- **Second occurrence of yesterday's lazy-proxy bug class**: `AuthController.login` (and `/auth/me`, and everywhere else `UserQueryService.rolesOf()` is used) called `Role::getCode`/`getPermissions()` on `UserRoleAssignment.role` after the transaction closed, throwing `LazyInitializationException` — `UserRoleAssignmentRepository.findByUserId` had never been given the `JOIN FETCH` that `findByUserIdIn` (the batch form, added yesterday for the N+1 fix) already had. **Login was completely broken** - every attempt 500'd, on the very first click-test this project has ever had. Fixed by adding `JOIN FETCH a.role` to the singular query too, since its only caller always reads the role afterward. This is the same root cause as yesterday's `orgScopeNode` fix (open-in-view disabled, lazy access after the session closes) recurring in a different association - worth a note that this class of bug will keep recurring anywhere a new lazy field gets read post-transaction until there's a lint rule or convention to catch it structurally, not just as they're each individually discovered.
- **`@PreAuthorize` denials have silently 500'd since the day they were written.** Spring Security's method-security interceptor throws `AuthorizationDeniedException` from *inside* the controller method invocation (AOP), which Spring MVC's own `@RestControllerAdvice` resolution catches before the exception ever reaches `JsonAccessDeniedHandler` (which only sees denials from the filter chain, per its own comment - method-security denials never reach the filter chain at all). `ApiExceptionHandler`'s catch-all `handleGeneric` was swallowing every one of them into a generic 500. This affected all 23 existing `@PreAuthorize` checks (both yesterday's and everything from EPIC-AST) from day one - nobody had ever actually triggered a denied check end-to-end to notice. Fixed with an explicit `@ExceptionHandler(AuthorizationDeniedException.class)` returning the same 403 problem+json shape `JsonAccessDeniedHandler` uses.

**US-USR-03 (permission checks enforced at the API, not just role-name checks) - built and click-tested:**
- `CurrentUser` gained a `permissions` field (with a 3-arg compatibility constructor so the ~18 existing test call sites didn't need touching) and a `hasPermission(String)` helper (`"*"` wildcard = Super Admin's blanket grant). `JwtService` now encodes/decodes a `permissions` claim alongside `roles`. `AuthController.login` computes the same role-permission union `/me` already did and puts it on the token.
- New `PermissionChecker` bean (`@perm.has('x:y')` in SpEL), reading `CurrentUser` off the `SecurityContext`.
- **All 23 `@PreAuthorize` checks across 8 controllers converted** from `hasAnyRole('ADMIN','SUPER_ADMIN')`/`hasRole('SUPER_ADMIN')` literals to `@perm.has(...)` permission-string checks (`users:read/write`, `roles:read/write`, `org:write`, `assets:write`, `asset-categories:write`). This is the actual point of the story: a custom role created through US-USR-02 (like `WAREHOUSE_LEAD`, created and click-tested today with only `["assets:write"]`) now actually grants API access - before today it couldn't, no matter what permissions it listed, because every check only recognized a fixed set of role-name string literals.
- **Migration V18** backfills `roles:read` and `asset-categories:write` onto `ADMIN`'s permission set - required because the old role-name checks let Admin through checks the seeded permission catalog (`V15`) never actually listed. Deliberately narrow: `asset-categories:write` is *not* given to `INVENTORY_MANAGER`, preserving the existing behavior that category configuration (unlike day-to-day asset CRUD) is Administrator-only - a real distinction the flat `assets:write` permission can't express, so a second permission string was needed rather than reusing one.
- 3 new tests (`PermissionCheckerTest`: grant/deny/wildcard). **Full suite: 68/68 passing.**
- **Click-tested end-to-end**, not just unit-tested: logged in as Super Admin, Admin, an Inventory Manager, and a custom-role user; confirmed Admin's `roles:read`/`asset-categories:write` (from V18) work, confirmed Inventory Manager can write assets but is correctly **403** (not 500, post-fix) on asset-categories, and confirmed the `WAREHOUSE_LEAD` custom role - a code no `@PreAuthorize` check has ever heard of - can create an asset purely because its permission set includes `assets:write`.

**Not started (still, within EPIC-USR):** US-USR-05 (System Operator technical-only restriction), US-USR-06 (self-approval block), US-USR-09 (SoD waivers) - unchanged from yesterday. Frontend doesn't read `/auth/me`'s `permissions` to hide controls yet - today's work was backend-only (the other half of US-USR-03's AC).

**Next session:** Wire the frontend to `/auth/me`'s `permissions` (closing the rest of US-USR-03's AC); or pick up US-USR-05/06/09; or note the recurring lazy-proxy bug class and consider whether a structural fix (e.g. an integration-test tier that boots a real Hibernate session, since Mockito unit tests structurally cannot catch `LazyInitializationException`) is worth the investment now that it's recurred twice.

---

## 2026-07-13, continued — "fix all bugs and blockers and resume Epic development"

Picked up the same day's thread per that instruction: closed the two biggest cited blockers (EPIC-ORG's missing hierarchy, US-USR-03's frontend half), pushed EPIC-ORG and EPIC-USR further, and — critically — click-tested every bit of it against live Postgres rather than stopping at green unit tests, which is what caught four more real bugs this pass.

**EPIC-ORG — built the hierarchy that's been blocking two other stories since yesterday:**
- **US-ORG-01** (multi-level hierarchy): new `org_level` table (4 seeded levels: Campus/Building/Floor/Room, `rank`-ordered) and `org_node` gained `parent_id`, `level_id`, `path` (materialized ancestor-id chain including self, e.g. `/campusId/buildingId/roomId/`), `room_variant` (V19). `path` is computed once at node creation and never recomputed - nodes aren't re-parented in this phase - which is what makes "this node and everything under it" a plain indexed `LIKE 'prefix%'` match instead of a recursive query. `OrgHierarchyService`/`OrgHierarchyController`: create (validates the child's level is exactly the parent's rank+1, rejects a root node at a non-zero rank, rejects a room-variant not configured on that node's level), get, list (flat, with path), delete (blocked with a structured dependent list - child nodes, assets, persons, users scoped to it).
- **US-ORG-02** (relabel level names): `PATCH /api/v1/org-levels/{id}` - only `name` is mutable, `code`/`rank` are fixed at seed time.
- **US-ORG-06** (Classroom/Laboratory Room variants): `OrgLevel.roomVariants` (a plain string list, same pattern as `Role.permissions`) - only the Room-rank level has any seeded; `OrgNode.roomVariant` must be one of its own level's list or is rejected.
- **US-ORG-03** (Department/Cost Center): new standalone `Department` entity + CRUD (V20). Deliberately **not** wired into Asset/Person yet - doing that touches the create/update DTOs, commands, and mappers of two already-click-tested epics, which is a separate, larger change than standing up the dimension itself. `DepartmentService.delete()`'s docstring says plainly there's no dependent-check yet, because nothing references a department yet - not a silently skipped AC, a genuinely not-yet-applicable one.
- **US-USR-09** (SoD waiver, EPIC-USR but built alongside ORG since it shares the sign-off-validation shape): new `SodWaiver` entity (V21) + `SodWaiverService`/`SodWaiverController`. Validates the signer actually holds `IT_SECURITY_OFFICER` and is never the same user recording the waiver (both click-tested: wrong-role signer and self-sign-off both correctly rejected with a 400 naming the reason). **Deliberately not built**: actually engaging the SoD-conflict reroute path (US-AUD-22) - there's no approval workflow yet for it to reroute. `SodWaiverRepository.existsByScopeAndActiveTrue` is the lookup that path will need, added now so it's not a schema change later.
- **Closed the actual blocker**: `OrgScopeGuard`/`UserScopeResolver` now do path-prefix matching, not exact-id - "scoped to Building A" now covers every Floor and Room under it. This flips **US-ORG-05 and US-USR-04 from Partial to Built** (dev-log status, not just code) - the exact-node-only limitation both stories' Partial status pointed at is gone. Click-tested concretely: created Building→Floor→Room under the seeded root, put a test asset in the Room, scoped a test user to the Building, and confirmed `GET /assets` and a direct `GET /assets/{id}` both return the three-levels-down asset.

**US-USR-03's other half - frontend permission-based UI gating (was the one named frontend gap):**
- JWT now carries a `permissions` claim alongside `roles` (`JwtService`, `AuthController.login`); `authStore.AuthUser` gained `permissions`, plus a `hasPermission(user, permission)` helper mirroring the backend's `CurrentUser.hasPermission` (wildcard `*` included).
- `AdminShell`'s nav switched from `requiresAnyRole: ['ADMIN','SUPER_ADMIN']` literals to `requiresPermission: 'users:read'`/`'roles:read'` - a custom role with those permissions now sees the right nav without a frontend code change. Same swap in `RoleListPage` (was checking `roles.includes('SUPER_ADMIN')` directly).
- Write controls hidden behind the same permissions the backend now enforces: "New User"/Deactivate (`users:write`), "New Role"/Edit/Delete (`roles:write`), "New Category"/Delete (`asset-categories:write`), "Register Asset"/Edit/status-change `Select` (`assets:write`). `tsc -b` and `oxlint` both clean.
- **This closes US-USR-03 fully** (API half from earlier today + this UI half) - dev-log status moves from Partial to Built.

**Four more real bugs found by click-testing, none caught by the (now) 88 passing unit tests:**
- **`OrgNode` had no `@PrePersist`.** Unlike every other mutable entity, it predates `BaseEntity` and was never migrated onto it - it still has its own `id`/`createdAt`/`updatedAt`, with nothing to populate them. First `POST /org-nodes` threw `DataIntegrityViolationException` (`created_at` NOT NULL violation). Fixed by giving `OrgNode` its own `@PrePersist`/`@PreUpdate`, mirroring `BaseEntity`'s exactly - a Mockito test stubbing `save()` to just echo the argument back can't catch this, since it never goes through a real JPA lifecycle callback.
- **`GET /assets` (list) threw `LazyInitializationException`** on `AssetCategory` - this project's first-ever call to the plain asset list endpoint (all prior click-testing only ever hit single-asset `GET`/`POST`). `AssetRepositoryImpl.search()`'s criteria query never fetched `category`/`status`/`orgNode`/`parentAsset`, all LAZY; `AssetMapper.toResponse` reads all four after the transaction closes. Fixed with explicit `.fetch()` calls (`JoinType.INNER` for the three non-null ones, `LEFT` for `parentAsset`) plus `.distinct(true)` as a safety net.
- **The same bug, in `GET /assets/{id}` and every asset-mutation endpoint.** `AssetQueryService.get()` used a plain `findById()` - same lazy fields, same crash once mapped. Root cause is that `AssetRegistrationService.register()` (create) never hits this because it explicitly loads `category`/`status`/`orgNode` as real objects before assigning them - proxies only appear when an already-persisted Asset is re-fetched by ID, which is exactly what `get()`/`update()`/`changeStatus()`/`assign()`/`unassign()`/`linkChild()`/`listChildren()` all do. Added `AssetRepository.findByIdWithAssociations()` (JOIN FETCH all four) and `findByParentAssetIdWithAssociationsOrderByCreatedAtAsc()` (same, for children), and swapped every one of those seven call sites - plus their optimistic-lock-conflict recovery paths, which return the same kind of object into `OptimisticLockConflictException`'s `currentResource` - from the plain lazy lookup. This is the third occurrence of the exact bug class flagged in yesterday's entry ("this class of bug will keep recurring... until there's a lint rule or convention to catch it structurally") - it just did, twice more, in one afternoon.
- **`AssetCategoryService.delete()`'s conflict used the literal errorCode `ORG_NODE_HAS_DEPENDENTS`** - a copy-paste artifact from before EPIC-ORG existed, and the exact code `AC-ORG-01-X` needed for *actual* org-node deletion once EPIC-ORG landed today. Renamed to `CATEGORY_HAS_DEPENDENTS` (no frontend or test depended on the old string) so `ORG_NODE_HAS_DEPENDENTS` means what the API spec says it means.

**Full backend suite: 88/88 passing** (68 from this morning + 12 `OrgHierarchyServiceTest` + 4 `DepartmentServiceTest` + 3 `SodWaiverServiceTest`, plus 1 new descendant-scope case in `AssetQueryServiceTest`). Frontend: `tsc -b` and `oxlint` both clean. Every new endpoint and every fix in this section was click-tested against live Postgres, not just unit-tested - see above for what that caught.

**Updated status:** EPIC-ORG now 3 built (US-ORG-01, 02, 06 counted as one build event, plus 04 from before), 1 partial→built (US-ORG-05), 2 not started (03 is a Partial now - the Department entity exists but isn't wired to Asset/Person). Net: **US-ORG-01/02/05/06 Built, US-ORG-03 Partial, US-ORG-04 Built (unchanged), US-ORG-05 Built** - only ORG's original "6 stories" scope now has just one Partial left. EPIC-USR: **US-USR-03 and US-USR-04 move from Partial to Built**; US-USR-09 added as Partial (recording/validation built, reroute-engagement deferred). US-USR-05/06 remain not started - US-USR-05's exception-path AC is now incidentally satisfied by the permission model (System Operator's permission set never included `assets:read`/`org:read` to begin with), but no dedicated technical-config settings endpoint exists for the happy-path AC to attach to, so it isn't claimed as Built.

**Deliberately not done, and why:** US-USR-05 (no technical-config settings API exists yet to gate - inventing one would be scope no story asked for), US-USR-06 (no transfer/disposal/audit submission concept exists yet to block self-approval against - same reasoning), Department↔Asset/Person wiring (real but separate scope, noted above), SoD waiver's reroute engagement (blocked on an approval workflow that doesn't exist).

**Next session:** Either wire Department into Asset/Person (closing US-ORG-03 fully) or move into a genuinely new epic now that R1's ORG/USR/AST work is nearly exhausted - EPIC-SEC has the most partials of any epic already touched (JWT-without-refresh, SLF4J-only audit log, min-length-only password policy) and no dedicated stories fully built, making it the next-highest-leverage target before jumping to R2 epics like LIF/AUD.

---

## 2026-07-13, continued again — EPIC-SEC: "continue the development and fix any blockers"

Picked up the previous entry's own recommendation and pushed EPIC-SEC from 0 fully-built stories to 4, closing all four of its cited partials down to two.

**New `com.iams.sec` package - the epic's first dedicated code, everything before this was a side effect of EPIC-USR's auth seam:**

- **US-SEC-04** (persistent, immutable Security & Access Log) - `SecurityEventLog` (append-only, same no-version/no-updated_at pattern as `AssetHistoryEvent`), `SecurityEventLogger` (the single writer, mirroring `AssetHistoryRecorder`'s shape), V22 migration. Wired into every event-producing call site that exists today: `AuthController.login` (LOGIN_SUCCESS/LOGIN_FAILURE), `OrgScopeGuard` (PERMISSION_DENIED, replacing yesterday's SLF4J-only line - the SLF4J line stays too, for local dev visibility without a DB round-trip), `UserProvisioningService.assignRoles` (ROLE_ASSIGNED), `UserDeactivationService.deactivate` (USER_DEACTIVATED). EXPORT/AUDIT_SUBMISSION event types named in the AC aren't in the enum yet - EPIC-CMP/EPIC-AUD, which would produce them, don't exist.
- **US-SEC-11** (search/filter the log) - `GET /api/v1/security-events`, gated `security:read` (V25 migration backfills that permission onto ADMIN, matching the story's own "As an Administrator" persona - SUPER_ADMIN/IT_SECURITY_OFFICER already had it via `*`/V15). Click-tested: a Viewer gets a correct 403.
- **US-SEC-09** (lock an account after 5 consecutive failed logins) - `AppUser` gained `failedLoginCount`/`lockedUntil` (V23); `UserLockoutService` (15-minute cooldown); wired into `AuthController.login` ahead of the BCrypt check (a locked account gets refused immediately - AC-SEC-09-X wants the lockout state surfaced, unlike username existence, so there's no timing-attack reason to pay BCrypt's cost first). Only a wrong *password* against a real account counts against the counter, not a correct password against a deactivated one - counting that would let an attacker learn deactivation status by watching the lockout threshold. Admin unlock: `POST /api/v1/users/{id}/unlock`. Self-service unlock isn't built - there's no email/notification system yet to deliver it through, noted rather than silently skipped. **Click-tested end-to-end**: 5 wrong-password attempts, 6th (even with the correct password) returned 423 with a distinct lockout message and `lockedUntil` timestamp, admin unlock, login working again immediately after.
- **US-SEC-05** (configurable password policy) - `PasswordPolicy` (single seeded row, V24), `PasswordPolicyService` (`GET`/`PATCH /api/v1/security/password-policy`, gated `security:write`), `PasswordValidator` (replaces `UserProvisioningService`'s old hardcoded 8-char-only floor). Every unmet rule becomes its own `ValidationErrorItem` (AC-SEC-05-X: "citing the specific unmet rules", plural) rather than stopping at the first failure. **Click-tested**: tightened the policy to min-12 + full complexity, a weak password came back with all 4 violations listed at once, a compliant one succeeded.

**Two more real bugs found by click-testing, neither caught by the (now) 106 passing unit tests:**
- **`SecurityEventLogRepository`'s first search implementation** (a plain JPQL `(:param IS NULL OR ...)` query) threw `InvalidDataAccessResourceUsageException: could not determine data type of parameter $5` - PGJDBC can't infer a bind parameter's type when its only appearances are both sides of an IS-NULL-guarded OR with a nullable `Instant`. First click-test of `GET /security-events` ever run. Fixed by converting to the JPA Criteria API (`SecurityEventLogRepositoryCustom`/`Impl`), the exact pattern `AssetRepositoryImpl` already uses for the same class of "several optional filters" query - a null filter there just never becomes a predicate, so PGJDBC never sees an ambiguous placeholder. This is a real, structural reason to prefer Criteria over JPQL string-templating for optional-filter searches in this codebase, not a one-off workaround.
- Everywhere `OrgScopeGuard` is constructed directly in tests (3 files) needed a new `SecurityEventLogger` mock added for the constructor's new 4th parameter - mechanical, not a design problem, but a reminder that `OrgScopeGuard` is now depended on by enough call sites that its constructor shape is effectively a small piece of shared infrastructure.

**Full backend suite: 106/106 passing** (88 before this session + 4 `PasswordPolicyServiceTest` + 5 `PasswordValidatorTest` + 2 `SecurityEventLoggerTest` + 7 `UserLockoutServiceTest`).

**Updated status:** EPIC-SEC goes from 0 Built/4 Partial/13 Not-started to **4 Built (US-SEC-04, 05, 09, 11) / 2 Partial (US-SEC-01 still no refresh token, US-SEC-14 still no service-account issuance flow) / 11 Not-started**. Overall: **28 Built / 5 Partial / 147 Not started** (180 total), up from 24/7/149.

**Deliberately not done, and why:** refresh tokens/logout-all (US-SEC-01) - a genuinely larger feature (rotation, a revocable store, a frontend refresh flow) that didn't fit alongside the four stories above; self-service account unlock (US-SEC-09's other clause) - no notification/email system exists to deliver it through; LDAP, MFA, session timeout, IP restriction, encryption-at-rest verification, service-account credential issuance, data export/erasure, break-glass access - all either need infrastructure (LDAP server, TOTP, email) or epics (EPIC-CMP) that don't exist yet, each a genuinely separate piece of work, not a small extension of what's here.

**Next session:** EPIC-SEC's remaining Must/R1 items (US-SEC-01 refresh tokens, US-SEC-06 session timeout, US-SEC-08 encryption verification) are the last real R1 gaps across all four touched epics. After those, every touched epic (AST/ORG/USR/SEC) will be at or near its ceiling without a new epic (LIF/AUD/etc.) actually starting - worth deciding explicitly next session whether to finish SEC's tail or start fresh in EPIC-AUD, the product's stated core differentiator, still completely untouched at 0/24.

---

## 2026-07-13, continued a third time — US-SEC-01 refresh tokens, closing US-USR-08

Picked up the previous entry's own recommendation: built refresh tokens, the one item that closed both a remaining EPIC-SEC Partial and (as a side effect) EPIC-USR's last-cited session-revocation gap.

**US-SEC-01 (revocable refresh tokens) - built and click-tested end-to-end:**
- `RefreshToken` (V26): rotation-based, not reuse-based - `RefreshTokenService.rotate()` revokes the presented row and issues a brand-new one on every exchange, so a stolen-then-replayed token is detectable (already revoked) rather than silently valid until its natural expiry. Only the SHA-256 hash is ever persisted, matching how passwords are never stored raw either.
- `POST /auth/refresh` (exchange, idle-timeout-checked - see below), `POST /auth/logout` (end this session), `POST /auth/logout-all` (end every session for the caller, authenticated). `LoginResponse` now carries both `accessToken` and `refreshToken`.
- **US-SEC-06 (session timeout), partially riding along**: `rotate()` refuses and revokes a refresh token that's gone unused longer than a configurable idle window (`iams.security.jwt.refresh-idle-timeout-minutes`, default 24h), logging `SESSION_EXPIRED`. Deliberately **not** claimed as fully Built: this only bites when a client actually attempts a refresh - the access token itself is still a stateless JWT valid for its own full configured lifetime (480 min default) regardless of activity, since shortening it now would break the frontend's existing no-silent-refresh login flow without also building that flow this session. Noted as a real architecture tradeoff, not silently glossed over.
- Deactivating a user now calls `refreshTokenService.revokeAll()` - **closes US-USR-08's session-revocation gap**: a deactivated user's refresh tokens stop working immediately, click-tested (deactivated user's stored refresh token correctly returned 401 on the next refresh attempt). The one part of that story's AC still open: their *access* token, if one was already issued, remains valid until its own natural expiry - there's no per-request revocation check for stateless JWTs, named explicitly in the code rather than left implicit.
- Frontend: `authStore` now holds the refresh token alongside the access token (memory-only, same as before - no persistence added); `AdminShell`'s sign-out calls `POST /auth/logout` best-effort before clearing local state, so logging out client-side also actually ends the session server-side. No silent-refresh-on-401 interceptor was built - that's a separate, larger frontend feature.
- 9 new tests (`RefreshTokenServiceTest`: issue, rotate success/reuse/expired/idle, revoke, revoke-all). **Full suite: 115/115 passing.**

**Two more real bugs found by click-testing, neither caught by the (now) 115 passing unit tests:**
- **`SecurityEventLogger.record()` had no transaction boundary of its own**, so when called from inside an already-`@Transactional` method that later throws - exactly the "log the denial/failure, then throw" pattern used by `OrgScopeGuard` (PERMISSION_DENIED), and the new `RefreshTokenService` (REFRESH_TOKEN_REUSE_DETECTED, SESSION_EXPIRED) - the event write joined the caller's transaction (Spring's default `REQUIRED` propagation) and got rolled back right along with it. The call site never saw an error; the row just silently never existed. First caught when a reuse-detection test showed 401 correctly but the event search came back empty. Fixed with `@Transactional(propagation = REQUIRES_NEW)` on `record()`, so a security-log write always commits independently of whatever business transaction triggered it - which is the actually-correct semantic for an audit log (you want the record of "this was denied" to survive even though the underlying operation was rolled back). This retroactively means **`PERMISSION_DENIED` events from `OrgScopeGuard` were never actually being persisted since EPIC-SEC's first session either** - re-verified live after the fix and confirmed they now are.
- **A plain `org.springframework.security.access.AccessDeniedException`** (thrown directly by `OrgScopeGuard.requireWithinScope()`, not via `@PreAuthorize`) fell through to the generic 500 handler, same root cause as the `@PreAuthorize`-denial 500 bug fixed earlier this same day - `ApiExceptionHandler` only had a handler for the newer `AuthorizationDeniedException`, and `OrgScopeGuard` throws the older, more general class directly. Since `AuthorizationDeniedException extends AccessDeniedException` (confirmed by inspecting the compiled class), the fix widens the existing handler to the parent type - one handler now correctly covers both the AOP-based `@PreAuthorize` case and this plain-application-code-throw case. Found by click-testing a genuinely out-of-scope single-asset fetch end-to-end for the first time - every prior scope-enforcement click-test in this project checked list-filtering or the in-scope path, never the single-entity denial's actual HTTP response.

**Updated status:** US-SEC-01 moves from Partial to Built. US-USR-08 stays Partial, but its cited gap narrows from "session/refresh-token revocation not implemented at all" to "refresh tokens now revoke immediately; the already-issued access token doesn't." The idle-timeout side effect of `rotate()` (see above) is real, tested, configurable behavior, so US-SEC-06 also moves from Not-started to Partial rather than being left at zero credit. EPIC-SEC: **5 Built (01, 04, 05, 09, 11) / 2 Partial (06, 14) / 10 Not started** (up from 4/1/12). Overall: **29 Built / 5 Partial / 146 Not started** (180 total), up from 28/5/147.

**Deliberately not done, and why:** US-SEC-06 fully (would need either much shorter access tokens + a frontend silent-refresh flow, or per-request session-state lookups that the stateless-JWT design deliberately avoids - a real architecture decision, not a small extension); access-token revocation on deactivation (same reasoning - no revocation list for stateless JWTs); self-service refresh-token unlock/rotation-visibility UI (no frontend surface for viewing/managing active sessions was built).

**Next session:** With US-SEC-01 done, EPIC-SEC's remaining R1 items (US-SEC-06 properly, US-SEC-08 encryption-at-rest verification, US-SEC-02 LDAP, US-SEC-03 MFA) all require either new infrastructure (LDAP server, TOTP) or an architecture change (shorter access tokens + frontend silent-refresh) rather than being incremental extensions of existing code - EPIC-SEC is close to its ceiling for "cheap" R1 progress. Genuinely worth starting EPIC-AUD next - the product's stated core differentiator, still 0/24, and the largest untouched epic in the backlog.

---

## 2026-07-13, continued a fourth time — "Fix all the bugs and blocker": first real browser testing

Every prior session's testing was curl/API-level only - every entry above notes "no browser-automation tool is available in this environment." Closed that gap: installed Playwright + Chromium (`npx playwright install chromium`, npm package installed into a scratch directory outside the repo, not added as a project dependency) and drove the live frontend (Vite dev server, proxying to the backend on a temporary alternate port since 8080 was occupied by an unrelated process - `vite.config.ts` was reverted back to its committed `8080` target before this session ended) with a real headless Chromium instance for the first time in this project's history.

**Two real bugs found by browser-testing, invisible to every prior curl-based click-test and to all 115 unit tests:**
- **Invalid HTML nesting on the Categories, Users, and Roles list pages** - React's DOM-nesting validator threw console errors ("`<div>` cannot be a descendant of `<p>`", "`<p>` cannot contain a nested `<p>`") on `CategoryConfigPage.tsx`, `UserListPage.tsx`, and `RoleListPage.tsx`. Root cause: MUI's `ListItemText` renders its `secondary` prop inside a `<Typography component="p">` by default, but all three pages pass a `<Stack>` (renders `<div>`) containing `Chip`s (render `<div>`) or a nested `<Typography>` (renders `<p>`) as that `secondary` content - block elements nested inside a paragraph tag, which is invalid HTML and (in React) a logged DOM-nesting warning that would have shown up as a real hydration-class bug in any SSR setup. Fixed by adding `slotProps={{ secondary: { component: 'div' } }}` to all three `ListItemText` usages, the MUI-documented pattern for exactly this case. Re-verified live: zero console errors across Assets, Categories, Users, and Roles after the fix, screenshots confirm all three pages render identically to before (the fix is invisible visually, only the invalid markup is gone).
- Confirmed **not** a bug, but worth recording so it isn't "rediscovered" as one next session: navigating with a full page load (`page.goto`, i.e. what a browser refresh or typed URL does) to any authenticated route correctly bounces to `/login`. This is `authStore`'s documented in-memory-only token design (see the comment in `authStore.ts`) working as intended, not a session bug - client-side nav (a sidebar click) preserves the session as expected.

**Click-tested three previously-never-exercised backend endpoints directly (curl), all passing with no bugs found:** `GET /api/v1/org-levels` (200, returns the 4 seeded levels), `PATCH /api/v1/departments/{id}` (200, updates and bumps version), `DELETE /api/v1/departments/{id}` (204, confirmed gone from the list), `POST /api/v1/sod-waivers/{id}/revoke` (200, `active` flips to `false`).

**Full backend suite: 115/115 passing**, unchanged by this session's fixes (frontend-only bugs; no backend code touched).

**Updated status:** No story moves Built/Partial/Not-started tier this session - the two bugs fixed were pre-existing defects in already-"Built" stories (US-ORG's category config UI, US-USR-01's user list UI, US-USR-02's role list UI), not new functionality. Overall RTM tally unchanged at **29 Built / 5 Partial / 146 Not started** (180 total). The real deliverable this session is a testing-capability gap closed, not a coverage-tally change: this project can now be verified by an actual rendered browser, not just HTTP responses.

**Deliberately not done, and why:** Playwright wasn't installed as a committed project dependency or wired into CI - it was a one-off verification pass in a scratch directory; making browser testing a repeatable, checked-in part of this project (a `frontend/e2e` suite, a project skill capturing the login-and-drive sequence) is real, separate work worth doing deliberately rather than as a byproduct of a bug-fix session.

**Next session:** The browser-testing gap being closed means future sessions can now catch frontend-only regressions (rendering, console errors, interaction bugs) that curl-based testing structurally cannot - worth using it again before claiming any future UI-touching story "Built." Substantively, EPIC-AUD (the product's core differentiator, still 0/24) remains the highest-leverage next target, unchanged from the previous session's recommendation.

## 2026-07-13, continued a fifth time — "Resume the development": EPIC-AUD, 0/24 to 13/24 Built

Picked up the previous entry's own recommendation and started EPIC-AUD - the product's own stated "core differentiator" (BR-05), the largest single epic in the backlog after EPIC-SEC, and completely untouched until now. Built a full vertical slice of the audit lifecycle end to end: define scope → freeze expected assets → assign auditors → scan/verify (single and batch) → submit with re-authentication and SoD-conflict detection → Department Head approve/reject → completion certificate and exception report, with findings immutable except via linked corrections. Backend-only, same pattern EPIC-SEC's first session used - no frontend page exists for any of it yet.

**New `com.iams.audit` package - five entities, five repositories, five services, one controller:**

- **`Audit`** (extends BaseEntity) - type, scope (org node and/or category, or an explicit asset list), status (`IN_PROGRESS`/`PENDING_APPROVAL`/`CLOSED` - see below for why only three), nominal/effective approver, submission signature, approval metadata. **`AuditExpectedAsset`** (append-only, no version/updated_*) - the frozen expected-asset snapshot (US-AUD-04), resolved once at creation by reusing `AssetRepositoryImpl.search()` for org-node/category scope or `AssetRepository.findAllById()` for an explicit list. **`AuditAssignment`** (extends BaseEntity) - auditor assignments that can end without being deleted, denormalizing the username at assignment time. **`AuditFinding`** (append-only, every "what was found" field `updatable=false`) - one row per resolved expected asset: `VERIFIED`/`MISSING`/`OUT_OF_SCOPE`/`SCOPE_CHANGED`, condition, remarks, verifier, timestamp, device. **`AuditFindingCorrection`** (append-only) - the only way condition/remarks ever change post-creation, mirroring `AssetHistoryEvent`'s correction-as-linked-row pattern exactly.
- **A deliberate two-step (not three-step) state machine**, documented on `AuditStatus`: the source stories describe "close scanning" (US-AUD-09) and "close after approval" (US-AUD-15) without a clear state between them, and R2 acceptance criteria in this document are explicitly provisional/derived, not ratified. This codebase folds them: `submit()` both classifies unverified expected assets Missing (US-AUD-09) and moves to `PENDING_APPROVAL`; `approve()` and closure (US-AUD-15) are the same event, since the stories describe them as one moment ("an approved and closed audit").
- **US-AUD-22 (SoD conflict detection) reused existing infrastructure rather than building new**: `SodWaiverRepository.existsByScopeAndActiveTrue` already existed for exactly this, built during an earlier session with a comment naming this story explicitly as its future caller. Added one new query (`findActiveByScopeOrderByCreatedAtDesc`) to resolve *which* waiver applies, since the reroute needs the signing officer's identity, not just a boolean. Click-tested end to end: a self-approval submission blocked with no waiver, then correctly rerouted to the waiver's signer once one was recorded, using the exact `"AUDIT_APPROVAL"` scope literal the seed data already used.
- **US-AUD-13's password re-authentication** reuses the same `PasswordEncoder` the login flow uses - wrong password leaves the audit fully unsubmitted (no state mutated above that check), correct password records a typed signature name alongside the re-auth event. Marked **Built**, not Partial, even though the story's AC also names MFA as an alternative: MFA doesn't exist anywhere in this codebase yet (US-SEC-03, a separate, already-tracked gap), and penalizing this story again for the same systemic absence would double-count one gap across two RTM entries.
- **Admin permission grant**: `ADMIN` never had `audits:read`/`audits:write` (V15 predates this epic) - added via `V28`, since US-AUD-24's own AC names "the Auditor assigned to the audit **or an Administrator**" as who may submit a correction.
- 34 new tests across `AuditServiceTest`, `AuditScanServiceTest`, `AuditWorkflowServiceTest`, `AuditFindingCorrectionServiceTest`, `AuditReportServiceTest`. **Full suite: 149/149 passing.**

**Two more real bugs found by live click-testing, neither caught by the 149 passing unit tests:**
- **A DB `CHECK` constraint (`V27`'s `chk_audit_scope_present`) was stricter than the actual rule.** It required an org-node or category scope, but `AuditService.create()` correctly also allows a third, explicitly-named case (FR-AUD-01's "asset list" scope) with both those columns null. The very first live audit-creation attempt using that exact case threw a 500. A `CHECK` constraint structurally can't see the `audit_expected_asset` rows the service layer produces, so it could only ever be a wrong, stricter subset of the real validation. Fixed in a new migration (`V29`, dropping the constraint) rather than editing the already-applied `V27` - editing an applied migration corrupts Flyway's checksum history, the same discipline every prior schema bug fix in this project has followed.
- **Rejecting a submitted audit left an orphaned, permanently-unfixable Missing finding.** `submit()` correctly auto-classifies unscanned assets Missing; `reject()` reset the audit's status and submission fields but never touched those Missing rows. Since findings are deliberately immutable with no re-scan-overwrites-existing path (US-AUD-24's whole point), a rejected-and-reopened audit could never actually verify that asset again - any rescan attempt hit `FINDING_ALREADY_RECORDED` forever. Found by click-testing the full reject-then-rescan cycle, a workflow shape no earlier epic in this project has had (there's no comparable "revert and retry" flow in AST/ORG/USR/SEC to have exercised this bug class before). Fixed by having `reject()` delete only the *system*-classified Missing rows it's undoing (identified by `verifiedByUserId IS NULL` - a real scan always has a verifier, so this can never touch recorded evidence). Re-verified live: reject, then rescan the same asset, now correctly returns `201` with a real `VERIFIED` finding.

**Updated status:** EPIC-AUD moves from 0 Built/0 Partial/24 Not-started to **13 Built (01, 02, 04, 05, 07, 08, 09, 10, 12, 13, 16, 22, 24) / 5 Partial (03, 14, 15, 17, 23) / 6 Not started (06, 11, 18, 19, 20, 21)**. Overall: **42 Built / 10 Partial / 128 Not started** (180 total), up from 29/5/146.

**Deliberately not done, and why:** photo evidence (US-AUD-11, no object storage exists anywhere in this codebase); offline sync (US-AUD-19) and statistical sampling (US-AUD-20, Should-priority) - both genuinely separate, larger features, not small extensions; cross-cycle analytics (US-AUD-18, needs reporting infrastructure that doesn't exist); escalation-on-timeout (US-AUD-14's other half) and automatic mid-audit scope-change detection (US-AUD-23's other half) - both need EPIC-LIF's transfer/dispose actions, which don't exist, so there is no "asset moved" event anywhere to hook into yet; reconciling a Missing asset outside an active audit (US-AUD-21, though the corrections mechanism built for US-AUD-24 could extend to it later); a completion-certificate PDF (JSON only); a frontend for any of this (deliberately deferred, same as EPIC-SEC's first session - backend-first, browser-test the frontend properly in a dedicated pass later).

**Next session:** Two productive directions now that EPIC-AUD has a solid backend core: (1) build its frontend (audit list/detail, scan-entry flow, approval queue) using the browser-testing discipline established two sessions ago, or (2) start EPIC-LIF (Asset Lifecycle Management, 16 stories, R2) - it directly unblocks two of EPIC-AUD's own Partials (US-AUD-14 escalation, US-AUD-23 automatic scope-change trigger) as a side effect, the same way EPIC-USR's auth seam once fed EPIC-SEC. R1 scope across EPIC-AST/ORG/USR/SEC remains close to fully exhausted, unchanged from prior sessions.

---

## 2026-07-14 — "Review and build all the EPICs": committed the backlog, then EPIC-LIF 0/16 to 6/16 Built

Asked to review and build across all epics. Everything from the five sessions above (2026-07-12 through 2026-07-13) had been sitting **uncommitted** in the working tree the whole time - only the original baseline-scaffold commit existed in git. Verified the full state first (149/149 backend tests, `tsc -b` + `oxlint` clean), then committed it as one checkpoint (293 files) before starting anything new, so five sessions of real, tested work weren't sitting unprotected in a working tree.

**Found a real, live regression while doing that:** a `com.iams.lifecycle` package (`TransferService`, `DisposalService`, `ApprovalRoutingService`, their domain entities/repositories, `application.yml`'s `iams.lifecycle.*` config) already existed on disk - fully written, compiling, well-documented EPIC-LIF scaffolding from a prior session that was never logged, never given a migration, never given a controller, and never committed. `ddl-auto: validate` means Hibernate checks every `@Entity`'s table at boot; with no migration creating `approval_delegation`/`asset_transfer_request`/`asset_disposal_request`, **the application could not start at all** - confirmed by actually booting it (`SchemaManagementException: missing table [approval_delegation]`). This had been true since before this session started; 149 passing Mockito unit tests never caught it because none of them boot a real Spring context. Committing broken code is exactly the failure mode `DEVELOPMENT_LOG.md`'s own click-testing discipline exists to catch, so fixing it became this session's first real task, and it happened to be next in line anyway (the previous entry's own recommendation was to start EPIC-LIF next).

**Completed the scaffold into a real, tested, click-tested feature (US-LIF-05/09/10/11/12/15 - Built; US-LIF-04/13 - Partial):**
- **`V30` migration**: `asset_transfer_request`, `asset_disposal_request`, `approval_delegation` tables - this alone fixes the boot regression.
- **`V31` migration**: `assets:restore` permission, granted to `ADMIN` only. US-LIF-12 is explicitly "As an Administrator, I want to restore..." - distinct from day-to-day `assets:write` that `INVENTORY_MANAGER` also holds, the same reasoning `V18` used to split `asset-categories:write` off for category configuration. Verified live: an Inventory Manager test user got a correct `403` on `/disposals/{id}/restore` while still getting `201` on creating transfers/disposals (`assets:write`) and `403` on approve/escalate (`approvals:write`, Department Head's permission).
- **`TransferController`/`DisposalController`/`ApprovalDelegationController`** (`/api/v1/transfers`, `/api/v1/disposals`, `/api/v1/approval-delegations`) plus DTOs and a shared `LifecycleMapper` - the API layer the service code had never had. Create is gated `assets:write` (Inventory Manager), approve/reject/escalate/delegate gated `approvals:write` (Department Head) - the service layer's `requireIsRoutedApprover` is what actually restricts action to *that* request's routed approver; the permission check is only the coarse gate.
- **25 new unit tests** (`TransferServiceTest`, `DisposalServiceTest`, `ApprovalRoutingServiceTest`) covering create validation, approve/reject/restore/escalate state transitions, and delegation routing/self-delegation rejection. **Full suite: 174/174 passing.**
- **Click-tested end-to-end against live Postgres**, not just unit-tested: booted the app (port 8081 - something unrelated already holds 8080 on this machine, same accommodation prior sessions made), logged in, and drove real HTTP flows: create-transfer → approve → confirmed the asset's `orgNodeId` actually changed and a `LOCATION_CHANGE` history row appeared; create-disposal(RETIRE) → approve → confirmed status became `RETIRED` → restore → confirmed status reverted to `IN_STORAGE`; reject-with-blank-reason → `400`; escalate-before-threshold → `409`; create-delegation → confirmed the *nominal* approver is correctly blocked (`403`) from approving while their delegate is active → revoke → confirmed the nominal approver's authority returns (`200`). Also created a real `INVENTORY_MANAGER` test user and confirmed the permission split live (create succeeds, approve/escalate/restore all correctly `403`).
- **Verified a real cross-epic effect, not just assumed it from reading code**: `TransferService.approve()`/`DisposalService.approve()` already called `AuditScopeChangeService.flagIfInActiveAudit()` (written during EPIC-AUD's session, which noted "EPIC-LIF's transfer/dispose actions don't exist yet" as exactly why US-AUD-23's automatic mid-audit scope-change detection was only Partial). That call was dead code until today - no API path could ever reach it. Click-tested directly: created an audit scoped to a room, transferred the room's asset elsewhere *without scanning it first*, and confirmed the audit's exception report now shows that asset as `SCOPE_CHANGED` - the exact behavior US-AUD-23's Partial status was waiting on. **This closes US-AUD-23 (Partial → Built)** as a direct side effect, independent of anything else this session touched in EPIC-AUD itself.

**Assessed, and deliberately not built this session, with why:**
- **US-LIF-01/02/03/16** (purchase requisition → PO → receiving, partial receipt/cancellation/vendor returns): zero existing domain code. A genuinely separate, large subsystem (new entities for request/PO/PO-line/receipt, not a small extension of anything built today) - the same class of decision prior sessions made about photo evidence or offline sync, not a shortcut.
- **US-LIF-06/07/08** (repair logging, scheduled preventive maintenance, unscheduled corrective maintenance): zero existing domain code, same reasoning - a real, separate feature area.
- **US-LIF-04's department half**: person-assignment already exists and is Built (EPIC-AST's `AssetAssignmentService`, prior session); assigning an asset to a *Department* has no path, since `Asset` carries no department reference and `Department` (EPIC-ORG) was itself noted as "not wired into Asset/Person yet" two sessions ago. Stays Partial for the same reason it already was.
- **US-LIF-14** (block person erasure while assets are assigned): `PersonService`'s own existing comment already says why this doesn't exist yet - "erasure is a later, approval-gated CMP-epic workflow, not a plain DELETE here." There is no erasure endpoint anywhere in this codebase to *have* a blocking check on. Building a blocking check ahead of the thing it blocks would mean inventing a stub for EPIC-CMP (untouched, 0 stories) under EPIC-LIF's name - real scope creep, not a shortcut. Stays Not-started, blocked on EPIC-CMP starting first.
- **US-LIF-13's full resolution order**: escalation to an active delegate is Built and click-tested; escalation to "Department Head's line manager" is not, because no management-hierarchy concept exists anywhere in this codebase to resolve it from (the existing `ApprovalRoutingService` Javadoc already named this gap before today) - falls back straight to any Administrator instead. Stays Partial.
- **Frontend**: none built for any of this, same backend-first precedent EPIC-SEC's and EPIC-AUD's first sessions set - a dedicated browser-testing pass later, not a shortcut taken today.

**Updated status:** EPIC-LIF moves from 0 Built/0 Partial/16 Not-started to **6 Built (05, 09, 10, 11, 12, 15) / 2 Partial (04, 13) / 8 Not-started (01, 02, 03, 06, 07, 08, 14, 16)**. EPIC-AUD: US-AUD-23 moves Partial → Built (14 Built / 4 Partial / 6 Not-started now, up from 13/5/6); US-AUD-14's escalation gap is unaffected (that's Audit's *own* escalation, not Transfer/Disposal's - not touched today). Overall: **49 Built / 11 Partial / 120 Not started** (180 total), up from 42/10/128.

**Next session:** EPIC-LIF's remaining Not-started items split into two independent tracks worth picking based on priority rather than sequence: (1) the procurement chain (US-LIF-01/02/03/16 - purchase request → PO → receiving), or (2) maintenance logging (US-LIF-06/07/08 - repair, preventive, corrective). Neither blocks the other. Separately, EPIC-CMP (Compliance & Data Privacy, 6 stories, still 0 touched) would unblock US-LIF-14 as a side effect once it exists, the same way today's session unblocked US-AUD-23. A frontend pass for EPIC-AUD + EPIC-LIF together (both backend-only so far) is also increasingly high-leverage now that two full epics' worth of API surface exists with nothing in the UI to drive it.
