## 2026-07-15, continued a fifth time — EPIC-INV frontend built, closing its last named gap; one more permission bug found by inspection before it ever shipped

Picked up the previous entry's own recommendation: built the frontend for all five EPIC-INV areas (items, warehouses, vendors, stock movements, manual adjustments) - the epic's Working Software Demonstration had explicitly named "no frontend exists" as its only real remaining gap, so this closes it rather than starting a new epic with EPIC-INV left API-only.

**Found and fixed a real permission-design bug in `ManualAdjustmentController` before writing a single line of frontend code against it** - the same "gated on the wrong permission" class this project has now hit five times, but this is the first instance caught by inspection rather than by a live 403. `GET` list/detail were gated `inventory:read` only; `approve()`/`reject()` were gated `approvals:write`. `DEPARTMENT_HEAD` holds `approvals:write`/`approvals:read` but never `inventory:read` - meaning a Department Head routed as approver could call `approve()` blind, by id, but could never list or review the request they were deciding on through the API. Fixed with this codebase's first OR-composed `@PreAuthorize` (`@perm.has('inventory:read') or @perm.has('approvals:read')`) - `approvals:read` already exists for exactly "see what's routed to me," the same reasoning `DEPARTMENT_HEAD`'s own role description already states. Caught this early specifically *because* the frontend build forced re-reading every endpoint's permission gate against who actually needs to call it, before wiring a page to it - worth doing deliberately for any future frontend pass, not just this one.

**New `frontend/src/features/inventory/` module**: `InventoryItemListPage` (list + create, with a live low-stock banner from `useLowStockQuery` - US-INV-04's dashboard-widget AC finally has a real, if minimal, home) and `InventoryItemDetailPage` (edit, per-warehouse/sub-location/lot balance table, Stock In/Out/Transfer dialogs, movement history, and costing-method-change history - the last of which only exists because of this session's own earlier work). `WarehouseListPage`, `VendorListPage` (create/deactivate plus a real purchase-history dialog backed by the `vendor_id` FK link built earlier), `ManualAdjustmentListPage` (request + approve/reject, built directly against the just-fixed permission gate). New `api/inventory/inventoryApi.ts` mirroring every backend DTO fresh rather than assumed. Five new nav entries in `AdminShell` - four gated the ordinary `requiresPermission: 'inventory:read'` way, and "Adjustments" gated by a new `requiresAnyPermission: string[]` field added to `NavItem` (the frontend's own nav-visibility equivalent of the backend's new OR-composed check, needed for the identical reason: Department Head must see this link too). `tsc -b` and `oxlint` both clean on the first pass - attributed to reading every backend DTO/controller/permission gate before writing the mirroring frontend code, the discipline that's kept every EPIC-CMP/AUD/LIF frontend pass clean before it.

**A second instance of the exact same bug class, caught before it ever ran**: while wiring `ManualAdjustmentListPage`'s create-request dialog, noticed its item/warehouse pickers would have called the `inventory:read`-gated `/inventory-items` and `/warehouses` endpoints unconditionally on page load - which a Department Head (now correctly able to reach this page to approve requests) would have hit immediately and 403'd on, just from navigating there, never touching the dialog. Fixed *before* browser-testing surfaced it: added `enabled` params to `useInventoryItemsQuery`/`useWarehousesQuery` and gated both on the dialog's own open state, mirroring the approver picker's already-correct `usePickableUsersQuery(createOpen)` gating right next to it.

**Browser-tested with Playwright** (reinstalled to a scratch directory again, never a committed dependency; Vite's proxy pointed at the session's alternate backend port 8081, reverted before finishing) as two real, non-admin roles:
- **`INVENTORY_MANAGER`**: created a warehouse, a vendor, and an item through the UI end-to-end; recorded a Stock In (50 @ $4.50) and a Stock Out (5), confirming the balance table showed exactly 45 with the right average cost; drove the balance down further through a manual-adjustment approval and a second Stock Out until it crossed the item's reorder level of 10, and watched the low-stock banner ("1 item below reorder level: Playwright FE Item (3/10)") appear with the exact right math, no manual refresh needed. Opened a vendor's purchase-history dialog and got the correct "no purchase orders yet" empty state.
- **`DEPARTMENT_HEAD`**: confirmed they see the "Adjustments" nav link (and correctly do *not* see Items/Warehouses/Vendors, which they have no permission for) - navigated to it, saw the pending request routed to them with zero console/network errors, and approved it successfully.
- **Zero console errors and zero failed network requests across every phase of both role's flows**, from first login to final approval.

**Full backend suite: 279/279 passing** (unchanged - the only backend change this session was the additive/corrective `@PreAuthorize` fix, no service logic touched). Frontend `tsc -b`/`oxlint` clean.

**Updated status:** No story-tier change - all 11 EPIC-INV stories were already Built; this session gave the epic real, browser-tested UI and fixed a permission-design bug in already-Built US-INV-05. Overall unchanged at **76 Built / 10 Partial / 94 Not started** (180 total). EPIC-INV is now genuinely complete in the sense its own Epic Completion Gate said it wasn't yet: a real Inventory Manager and a real Department Head can use it end-to-end through the actual application, not just the API.

**Deliberately not done this session, and why:** did not audit every other controller in the codebase for the same OR-composed-permission need beyond the one demonstrated broken here - fixed a real, found gap, not every place the pattern could theoretically recur (the permission-matrix audit two sessions ago already did the systematic version of this exercise once; this is a second, narrower instance found by a different method - building against the endpoint rather than grepping for it). Expiring-lots view has no dedicated frontend page yet (the query/endpoint exists and is tested, US-INV-09 stays Built per the same "query exists, no dashboard yet" precedent already applied to low-stock) - a real, small, named follow-up.

**Next session:** EPIC-INV is now complete end-to-end, front and back. Live options: (1) a dedicated expiring-lots view (small, the query already exists); (2) start a fresh, entirely untouched R2 epic (NTF/DSH/RPT/SRC/ANL) - EPIC-DSH would give both US-INV-04's low-stock and US-AUD-17's dashboard needs a real shared home, making it an increasingly natural next pick; (3) the CI/CD pipeline gap, flagged three sessions running now as real, pre-existing, project-wide debt.

## 2026-07-15, continued a sixth time — the CI/CD pipeline gap, closed after being flagged three sessions running

Picked up the debt named at the end of the last three entries rather than deferring it a fourth time: this project had a Definition-of-Done checklist item ("CI pipeline passes") that no session had ever actually been able to satisfy, because no pipeline existed to run.

**Checked first, rather than assumed: this repo has no GitHub remote at all** (`git remote -v` is empty, no `.github/` directory existed). A GitHub Actions workflow is inert config until code reaches GitHub - adding the workflow file is a safe, local, fully reversible change; actually creating a remote and pushing this project's code externally is a materially different, consequential decision (external visibility, a new piece of shared infrastructure) that wasn't made here and wasn't asked for. This session did the former only: added `.github/workflows/ci.yml`, ready to run the moment this repository is ever pushed anywhere, without taking that step itself.

**Two independent jobs, mirroring exactly what's already been run locally every session, not inventing a parallel CI-only process:**
- **Backend**: `actions/setup-java` (Temurin 21, matching `pom.xml`'s `<java.version>`) + a Postgres 16-alpine service container using the *exact* image/credentials `docker-compose.yml` already defines, so CI mirrors local dev rather than drifting into its own bespoke setup. Runs `mvn -B clean test` - the full 279-test suite against a real, migrated Postgres instance, the same "click-tested against live Postgres, not mocked" standard every session's own manual testing has already held itself to.
- **Frontend**: `actions/setup-node` (20) + `npm ci` + `npm run lint` (oxlint) + `npm run build` (`tsc -b && vite build` - typecheck and a real production bundle in one step, not just a typecheck).

**Verified every command in the workflow actually passes, rather than trusting the YAML would work untested**: ran `mvn -B clean test` locally (the literal CI command) - 279/279 passing. Ran a clean `npm ci` to reproduce CI's from-scratch install (not just reusing the already-populated local `node_modules`, which can mask a missing-from-lockfile dependency) - and this is exactly what caught a real, if mundane, problem: the first `npm ci` attempt left `node_modules` in a corrupted, partially-deleted state (`ENOTEMPTY` on a stale directory, most likely a Windows file-lock race with a `vite build` still exiting from the moment before). Diagnosed by symptom (`oxlint` suddenly "not recognized", `node_modules` sitting at 97 entries instead of the expected ~140) rather than guessed at, fixed by clearing `node_modules` outright (fully reproducible from `package-lock.json`, nothing of value lost) and reinstalling clean - 139 packages, 0 vulnerabilities, `npm run lint`/`npm run build` both green afterward.

**One real, pre-existing finding surfaced along the way, not fixed (out of scope for adding a pipeline, worth naming rather than burying):** `vite build`'s own output warns the production bundle is a single ~988 KB chunk (289 KB gzipped) with no code-splitting anywhere in this project. Real technical debt, not a regression from today - noted here so it doesn't need rediscovering, not addressed now.

**Extended the same pipeline to the other two Quality-Gate line items the charter names alongside "CI passes" - dependency scan and security scan - rather than leaving them as a second round of deferred debt right after closing the first:**
- **Dependency scan**: `npm audit --audit-level=high` added as a CI step (verified clean: 0 vulnerabilities against the freshly-reinstalled `node_modules` above) plus a new `.github/dependabot.yml` covering all three real dependency surfaces this project has - Maven (`/backend`), npm (`/frontend`), and the CI workflow's own GitHub Actions versions - weekly, opening PRs rather than failing builds, since a new CVE in a transitive dependency shouldn't block someone else's unrelated same-day work the way a broken test should.
- **Security scan (SAST)**: new `.github/workflows/codeql.yml`, GitHub's own CodeQL analyzing both `java-kotlin` and `javascript-typescript` as a matrix, on push/PR to main plus a weekly schedule so a scan still runs on a quiet week. Uses GitHub's standard, documented template structure - **not independently executable locally the way `mvn test`/`npm run build` were** (CodeQL's analysis engine requires GitHub's own Actions runner infrastructure), so unlike every other claim in this entry, this one is honestly unverified beyond "the YAML parses and follows the documented format exactly" (checked with a plain `yaml.safe_load` against all three new files, all three OK) - it will only be proven correct the first time this repository actually has a remote and a workflow run to look at.

**Updated status:** No story-tier change - this is infrastructure, not a backlog story. Overall unchanged at **76 Built / 10 Partial / 94 Not started** (180 total). What changes going forward: every future session's Definition-of-Done "CI pipeline passes," "dependency scan," and "security scan" line items are now real, checkable claims the moment this repository has a remote, not standing caveats repeated indefinitely.

**Deliberately not done this session, and why:** did not create a GitHub remote or push - a real decision with external consequences (visibility, a new piece of shared infrastructure to maintain) that belongs to the user, not something to make unilaterally while closing an internal tooling gap; this also means CodeQL's own correctness (see above) can't be confirmed until that happens. Did not add bundle code-splitting - a real but separate performance concern surfaced as a side effect of verifying the build, not the task at hand.

**Next session:** With CI/CD, dependency scanning, and static security analysis all now real (pending only a remote to actually run against), live options: (1) a dedicated expiring-lots view (small, US-INV-09's query already exists); (2) start a fresh R2 epic (NTF/DSH/RPT/SRC/ANL) - EPIC-DSH particularly natural given US-INV-04/US-AUD-17's shared dashboard need; (3) the bundle code-splitting finding from this session, a real but low-urgency performance item.

---

## 2026-07-15, continued a seventh time — EPIC-DSH built from scratch, 0/7 to 7/7 Built, front and back in one session

Picked up the previous entry's own recommendation and started EPIC-DSH (Dashboard, BR-08) - the natural next epic since US-INV-04's low-stock widget and US-AUD-17's audit dashboard had both been waiting for a real home. Unlike every prior epic's backend-first first session, this epic went **backend + frontend + browser-tested in one sitting** - justified because EPIC-DSH is mostly an aggregation layer over queries prior epics already built and click-tested (low-stock, audit progress, maintenance-due, asset history), not new domain machinery.

**New `com.iams.dashboard` package - one entity, one repository, one criteria-query component, two services, one controller (migration V39):**

- **Eight endpoints under `/api/v1/dashboard`, all gated on `dashboards:read`** - the permission V15 seeded onto VIEWER ("read-only access to dashboards and reports" is that role's entire reason to exist) **that no endpoint had ever used** - the same seeded-but-never-referenced class as the `MISSING` asset status found two sessions ago. V39 grants it to ADMIN/INVENTORY_MANAGER/AUDITOR/READONLY_AUDITOR/DEPARTMENT_HEAD (every role whose DSH story or V15 role description names dashboards); EMPLOYEE_VOLUNTEER deliberately excluded (no DSH story names them). **Deliberate design decision, documented in `DashboardTile`'s Javadoc**: tiles ride on the single `dashboards:read` permission rather than each source module's own read permission, because these are org-scoped *aggregates* and VIEWER (board member/finance officer persona) exists precisely to see them without holding `assets:read`/`audits:read`/`inventory:read` detail access. Detail navigation stays gated by the underlying permissions in the UI.
- **`DashboardQueries`** (US-DSH-01/03/05): Criteria-API aggregates - asset count + per-category/per-status group-bys, warranty/insurance expiration windows, recent asset-history events - each taking the caller's org-scope path prefix as an optional predicate *inside the query* (never post-filtered, so a scoped caller's feed can't be under-filled). Criteria, not JPQL templates, per the structural answer `SecurityEventLogRepositoryImpl` established for optional-filter queries against PGJDBC. Scalar tuples where a widget needs three columns, not six hydrated object graphs.
- **`DashboardService`**: merges warranty + insurance + maintenance-due into one date-sorted expirations list (US-DSH-03) - maintenance includes already-overdue schedules on purpose (an overdue service must not vanish) while warranty/insurance are window-only (an already-expired policy is a fact, not an upcoming lapse); audit completion (US-DSH-02) reuses `AuditReportService.dashboard()` (US-AUD-17) with per-audit percentage plus an average that is **null, not 0, when no active audits exist** (the AC's empty state); low stock (US-DSH-04) delegates to `InventoryStockService.lowStockItems()` unchanged. **Staleness policy documented in the service Javadoc** (the "documented cache policy" US-DSH-01/02's ACs cite): there is deliberately no cache - live reads trivially satisfy both ACs' staleness ceilings (5 min / 30 s) without cache infrastructure nothing else needs yet; if one is ever added, those ceilings are its contract.
- **`DashboardPreference`** (US-DSH-06, V39): one row per user, tiles as a jsonb array of enum names. "No row yet" = the default set (all available tiles); an existing row with an empty array = a deliberate, saved "show nothing" - the two states are distinguishable on purpose. Always operates on the *calling* user; no admin path to another user's layout exists, so there is no id parameter to abuse. PUT is gated `dashboards:read`, not a `:write` - it only ever writes the caller's own layout row. Unknown tile names are rejected at JSON deserialization (the request DTO types the list as the enum - `AssetCondition`'s established boundary pattern); duplicates collapse first-occurrence-wins.
- **`Audit.scheduledDate`** (nullable, V39): US-DSH-05's calendar AC ("audits scheduled in the next 30 days... on its scheduled date") needed a date to plot, and Audit never had a scheduling concept - created straight into IN_PROGRESS. Optional at creation, threaded through request→command→service→mapper→response, plotted by `GET /dashboard/audit-calendar`, scope-filtered exactly like `AuditService.list()` (including its documented US-AUD-03 category-scope pass-through). Same small cross-epic-extension class as `purchase_order.vendor_id`.
- **13 new unit tests** (`DashboardServiceTest`, `DashboardPreferenceServiceTest`): scope-prefix pass-through, percentage math (including empty-expected-set = 100%), null-average empty state, three-kind merge sorted with an overdue maintenance item first, lookahead/limit boundary rejection, dedupe order, saved-empty-vs-never-configured, update-not-duplicate. **Full backend suite: 292/292 passing** (279 + 13).

**Frontend, same session**: new `features/dashboard/` (types mirrored 1:1 from `DashboardDtos.java` read fresh, `useDashboardQueries` hooks, `DashboardPage`) + `api/dashboard/dashboardApi.ts`. Tiles render in the user's saved order; each widget's query is `enabled`-gated on its tile actually being selected (the discipline the approver-picker bug class established) so a removed tile costs nothing on load. Configure dialog with checkboxes per available tile; canonical-order preservation on re-add. Every empty state is a real sentence, not a blank panel. New "Dashboard" nav entry (first item, `requiresPermission: 'dashboards:read'`), new `/dashboard` route. The audit-create dialog gained an optional "Scheduled date" field feeding the calendar. `tsc -b` and `oxlint` clean.

**Click-tested end-to-end against live Postgres** (Postgres 18 on this machine's own port 5432 - noticed and worth recording: the `docker-compose` Postgres 16 container is *not* what the app talks to; a native PostgreSQL 18.4 owns port 5432 on this machine, confirmed by Flyway's own boot log naming 18.4, so `docker exec ... psql` queries an empty shadow database - verify data through the app's API or the native instance, not the container): all six widgets returned real data as admin; three fresh test users created (`dsh_viewer` VIEWER, `dsh_im` INVENTORY_MANAGER, `dsh_dh_bldga` DEPARTMENT_HEAD scoped to Building A). **US-DSH-07 proven with real data, not assumed**: the scoped DH's asset summary showed exactly 1 (the only Building A asset) where unscoped users see 4, their activity feed contained only that asset's events, and their audit list only Building-A/unscoped audits. Preferences: save → reload → persisted; dedupe verified; per-user isolation verified (viewer's subset never affected admin's default). Calendar: created an audit scheduled +10 days, appeared for admin and the in-scope DH.

**Adversarial pass, one real bug found and fixed immediately**: unauthenticated → `401` on all 8 endpoints; `COMPLIANCE_OFFICER` (no `dashboards:read`) → `403` on every endpoint tried; `withinDays=-1`/`9999`, `limit=0`/`500`, bogus tile name, `tiles:null`, malformed JSON → all `400`; empty tile list → `200` (a deliberate choice, distinguishable from never-configured). **The bug: `?withinDays=abc` returned `500`, not `400`** - `MethodArgumentTypeMismatchException` (Spring's query-param type-conversion failure) had no handler in `ApiExceptionHandler` and fell through to the generic 500. Pre-existing for *every* typed `@RequestParam` in the codebase (e.g. `/maintenance-schedules/due?withinDays=abc` 500s identically) - EPIC-DSH was just the first adversarial pass to throw a non-numeric string at a typed param. Fixed with a dedicated handler (400, names the parameter), re-verified live.

**Browser-tested with Playwright** (scratch-directory install again, never a committed dependency; Vite proxy pointed at this session's port-8081 backend, reverted before finishing) as three real roles: **Phase 1 (`dsh_im`)** - all six tiles render with live data (4 assets, 36% across 16 audits, low-stock row, calendar entry). **Phase 2 (`dsh_viewer`)** - configured a 2-tile subset via the dialog, unchecked tiles disappeared, and the subset survived a *fresh login in a new browser context* - deliberately not `page.reload()`, which correctly bounces to /login since tokens are memory-only by documented design (the test's first draft used reload and failed for exactly that reason; the documented posture, working). **Phase 3 (`dsh_dh_bldga`)** - asset summary showed 1 not 4, feed showed only Building-A events, calendar showed the Building-A audit. **Zero console/network errors across all three phases**; screenshots reviewed, not just captured.

**Updated status:** EPIC-DSH moves from 0 Built/0 Partial/7 Not-started to **7 Built (01, 02, 03, 04, 05, 06, 07) / 0 Partial / 0 Not-started - complete front-to-back in its first session**. US-AUD-17 stays Partial but its "no frontend page" half is now narrower (the audit-completion tile is a real UI surface with live per-audit progress; its exception counts and a recent/closed section remain unbuilt). US-INV-04's dashboard-widget AC now has its intended home (the item-list banner from the INV session remains too). Overall: **83 Built / 10 Partial / 87 Not started** (180 total), up from 76/10/94.

**Deliberately not done, and why:** no cache layer (documented above - live reads satisfy both staleness ACs; adding Caffeine for a bound zero already meets is speculative infra); AMC expirations as a distinct kind (US-AST-08's own model tracks AMC through the warranty fields - "AMC-specific modeling not separately verified" per its original entry - so the WARRANTY kind is honestly also the AMC surface until AST models them apart); drag-to-reorder tiles (the checkbox dialog satisfies "select a subset and save"; canonical order is preserved on re-add - reordering is polish no AC names); `EMPLOYEE_VOLUNTEER` dashboard access (no DSH story names them; their V15 description says no administrative access); a dedicated calendar-grid month view (the ACs ask that scheduled audits "appear on its scheduled date" - a date-sorted list with date chips satisfies this; a full month grid is presentation polish).

**Next session:** Three of the five untouched R2 epics remain fully unstarted: EPIC-NTF (Notifications, 10), EPIC-RPT (Reporting, 15), EPIC-SRC (Search, 5), plus EPIC-ANL (4) and the big EPIC-PLAT (16, R1-R3 enablers). EPIC-RPT is the natural next pick - DEPARTMENT_HEAD/INVENTORY_MANAGER/VIEWER all already hold `reports:read` from V15 (another seeded-but-unused permission, the exact pattern `dashboards:read` just closed), and several reports are the same aggregate-over-existing-queries shape this session just proved cheap. Alternatively US-AUD-11 (photo evidence) remains the standing infra-session option with MinIO still provisioned and unused.

## 2026-07-15, continued an eighth time — EPIC-RPT started, 0/15 to 6 Built / 1 Partial: the report backbone and every list report existing queries could already serve

Picked up the previous entry's own recommendation and started EPIC-RPT (Reporting, BR-10). Requirement analysis split the 15 stories into three clusters: **(A)** six list reports whose underlying queries prior epics already built and click-tested (register, scoped inventory, employee assets, expiry, movements, security log), **(B)** five aggregate reports (loss/vendor/audit-compliance/depreciation/maintenance), and **(C)** genuinely infra-heavy items (Excel/PDF export, background export jobs, scheduled email delivery, batch labels, the Could-priority ad hoc builder). This session built the backbone plus all of Cluster A, backend and frontend, same one-sitting pattern EPIC-DSH just proved workable for aggregation-layer epics.

**New `com.iams.report` package (migration V40):**

- **`TabularReport`** - the deliberate architectural bet of this epic: every report is a titled table of string cells. One shape means one generic CSV exporter, one generic frontend renderer, and zero per-report serialization code; Cluster B's aggregates and the eventual Excel/PDF exporters plug into it unchanged.
- **`CsvExporter`** (US-RPT-12's CSV leg): RFC 4180 - quoting, embedded-quote doubling, CRLF - **with a UTF-8 BOM**, because Excel misreads BOM-less UTF-8 CSVs as the legacy codepage and silently mangles non-ASCII asset names, which for a report handed to a board meeting is a correctness bug, not cosmetics. Unit-tested at the byte level (BOM bytes, quoting, null cells).
- **Five endpoints on `reports:read`** - V15's second seeded-but-never-consumed permission (INVENTORY_MANAGER/DEPARTMENT_HEAD/VIEWER have held it since V15), now with its first consumers; V40 grants it to ADMIN (US-RPT-03/14 name an Administrator) and AUDITOR/READONLY_AUDITOR (US-RPT-08). **The one exception, by the story's own AC: `/reports/security-events` is gated `security:read`, not `reports:read`** - US-RPT-14 explicitly refuses a Viewer, consistent with US-SEC-11's live view.
- **US-RPT-01/02 (`/reports/asset-register`)**: reuses `AssetRepository.search()`'s existing fetch-joined, scope-prefixed query, walking pages of 500 server-side into one report. An explicit `orgNodeId` narrows to that node's subtree ("department, room, or building" - all org-hierarchy nodes; a Department-*dimension* report stays blocked on US-ORG-03's known Department-not-wired-to-Asset gap, named rather than papered over). **A requested node outside the caller's own scope is refused (403), not silently intersected** - pretending the answer is "empty" would misreport reality.
- **US-RPT-03 (`/reports/employee-assets`)**: current assignments via the existing `findByAssignedToPersonId`, with the **assignment date pulled from the history trail** (latest `ASSIGNMENT_CHANGE` per asset, one batch query for the whole set, not one lookup per asset). Zero assignments renders an explicit empty report, not an error.
- **US-RPT-05 (`/reports/expiry`)**: delegates to `DashboardService.expirations()` (US-DSH-03, built earlier today) - warranty/AMC/insurance plus maintenance due, merged and date-sorted, report-sized 90-day default window.
- **US-RPT-07 (`/reports/asset-movements`)**: new `ReportQueries.movements()` criteria query - `LOCATION_CHANGE` history events in a date range (inclusive end date, unit-tested to the exact UTC instant), chronological, org-scoped inside the query, with from/to nodes, actor, and timestamp per the AC.
- **US-RPT-14 (`/reports/security-events`)**: the existing `SecurityEventLogRepository.search()` (US-SEC-11) rendered through the same tabular/CSV pipeline with all its filters.
- **12 new unit tests** (`CsvExporterTest`, `ReportServiceTest`). **Full backend suite: 304/304 passing** (292 + 12).

**Frontend, same session**: one generic `ReportsPage` (new `features/reports/`, `api/reports/reportApi.ts`) - a report picker (the security report only offered to `security:read` holders), per-report parameter controls with the enabled-gated picker discipline, a generic sticky-header table off the uniform shape, an explicit "ran successfully and found nothing" empty state, and **CSV download through the authenticated axios client as a blob** - a plain `<a href>` would drop the Authorization header, since tokens are memory-only by design. New "Reports" nav entry gated `reports:read`. `tsc -b`/`oxlint` clean.

**A second member of the DSH session's bug family, found by this session's adversarial pass and fixed immediately: a *missing* required query parameter returned `500`, not `400`.** `MissingServletRequestParameterException` had no handler - the exact sibling of the `MethodArgumentTypeMismatchException` gap fixed hours earlier (that one covered malformed values; this one covers absent ones). Pre-existing for every required `@RequestParam` in the codebase; fixed in `ApiExceptionHandler` (400, names the parameter), re-verified live (`/reports/employee-assets` with no `personId` → 400 "Parameter 'personId' is required.").

**Click-tested against live Postgres** (also recorded this session, for future DB spelunking: the app's Postgres is a **native PostgreSQL 18.4 on the host's port 5432**, confirmed by Flyway's own boot log - the docker-compose Postgres 16 container is a shadow with an empty database; verify data through the app or the native instance, never `docker exec psql`): register JSON+CSV as admin (4 rows, BOM + attachment headers verified); employee-assets for a real person showing the true `ASSIGNMENT_CHANGE` timestamp; expiry at 365d (7 rows) and movements over 30d (7 rows, from/to/actor/timestamp). Scope both ways as the Building-A-scoped Department Head: register narrowed to 1 row, and an explicit out-of-scope `orgNodeId` request → `403`. Adversarial: `401` unauthenticated on all five; VIEWER → `200` on reports, **`403` on security-events (US-RPT-14's AC, verified live)**; COMPLIANCE_OFFICER (no `reports:read`) → `403`; inverted date range, oversized lookahead, non-UUID and missing `personId`, malformed date → all `400` (the last two only after this session's handler fix); unknown person → `404`.

**Browser-tested with Playwright as three real roles, zero console/network errors**: a Viewer ran the Asset Register, confirmed the Security & Access Log is not even offered in their picker, and downloaded a CSV whose bytes were verified (BOM + header); an Inventory Manager ran expiry at 365d (7 rows) then 1d (0 rows - the window-change AC observed live) and the movements report; admin ran the security-log report. Screenshots reviewed - the Viewer's nav correctly shows only Dashboard/Reports/Assets/Categories.

**Updated status:** EPIC-RPT moves from 0/0/15 to **6 Built (01, 02, 03, 05, 07, 14) / 1 Partial (12: CSV export real and byte-verified for every report; Excel/PDF and the background-job path for very large exports not built) / 8 Not started (04, 06, 08, 09, 10, 11, 13, 15)**. Overall: **89 Built / 11 Partial / 80 Not started** (180 total), up from 83/10/87 - Not-started is now below half the backlog for the first time.

**Deliberately not done, and why:** Excel/PDF export (US-RPT-12's other legs) - real library dependencies (POI, a PDF renderer) worth their own deliberate session, not a bolt-on; background export jobs - no async-job infrastructure exists anywhere in this codebase yet; US-RPT-13 (scheduled email delivery) - needs both a scheduler and an email system, neither exists (same standing gaps named since EPIC-SEC's lockout session); US-RPT-11 (batch labels) - the per-asset label pipeline exists but batch PDF assembly is its own piece of work; Cluster B's five aggregate reports - each is real query-design work, honestly a second session, not squeezable into this one; US-RPT-15 - Could priority. CSV builds in memory (register CSV walks pages server-side but accumulates rows before writing) - fine at current data sizes, a named streaming follow-up if registers ever get huge.

**Next session:** EPIC-RPT's Cluster B (US-RPT-04 loss report, 06 vendor/purchase, 08 audit compliance, 09 depreciation, 10 maintenance history) - five aggregate reports that now plug into a proven backbone, the highest-leverage continuation. After that, the epic's remainder is genuinely infra-shaped (Excel/PDF, scheduling+email, batch labels) and worth pairing with US-AUD-11's object-storage session or an eventual EPIC-NTF start, where the email infrastructure would serve two epics at once.

---

## 2026-07-15, continued a ninth time — EPIC-RPT Cluster B: the five aggregate reports, US-RPT-04/06/08/09/10 Built

Picked up the previous entry's own recommendation: the five aggregate reports, each plugging into the session-old `TabularReport` backbone unchanged - no new export code, no new frontend renderer, exactly the payoff that backbone was built for.

**Backend - five new `ReportService` methods, two new `ReportQueries` criteria queries, five new `reports:read` endpoints (no new migration needed):**

- **US-RPT-04 (`/reports/loss`)**: every Missing or Verified-but-damaged finding across every audit (same damage-condition set `AuditReportService` uses for exceptions, so a "Damaged" loss row means exactly what an audit exception means), each row naming its source audit, newest first, optional date range, org-scoped via the asset's node inside the query. **A modeling correction found by the compiler, worth recording: `AuditFinding` has no `createdAt` - its universal timestamp is `verifiedAt`, set on persist even for system-classified MISSING rows** (its own append-only design predates BaseEntity's audit columns); the report filters and sorts on that, with a comment explaining why.
- **US-RPT-06 (`/reports/vendor-purchases`)**: item-level PO-line detail grouped by vendor with a subtotal row per vendor and a grand total - "totals and item-level detail break down by vendor" in one table. Vendor identity prefers the real `Vendor` FK (US-INV-07) and falls back to the order's free-text vendor name, which predates the Vendor entity. Deliberately not org-scoped: procurement carries no org node anywhere in this codebase, stated in the query's Javadoc rather than silently pretending otherwise. Subtotal/total math unit-tested to the cent and re-verified live (six vendors, grand total 11,515.00 matched by hand).
- **US-RPT-08 (`/reports/audit-compliance`)**: completion rate (closed/total), exception rate (closed audits with ≥1 exception / closed), and on-time rate across a period, with per-audit rows underneath the three summary rows. **The honest on-time definition**: computed only over audits that have both a scheduled date (optional since V39) and a submission - an audit with no scheduled date has no deadline to be late against, and the denominator is stated on the summary row itself ("0/0 audits with a scheduled date and a submission" in today's live data, which is exactly the truth). Open audits are listed with live status and "n/a (open)" exceptions - never counted as complete, per the AC.
- **US-RPT-09 (`/reports/depreciation`)**: NBV per in-scope asset as of the report date via the existing `DepreciationService.compute()` (FR-AST-16). An unconfigured asset is explicitly `NOT_DEPRECIATED` (never a misleading zero, the AC's own words); an asset whose configured method the engine can't compute yet (DECLINING_BALANCE throws) **degrades to its own `UNSUPPORTED` row instead of failing the whole report** - the same per-row-degradation principle US-RPT-11's batch AC states, applied here deliberately. Live-verified both paths: all four test assets correctly `NOT_DEPRECIATED`, then a straight-line override configured on one (1.6M cost, 10% salvage, 36 months, in service 2026-01-15) produced accumulated 280,000.00 / NBV 1,320,000.00 - checked by hand, correct to the cent.
- **US-RPT-10 (`/reports/maintenance-history`)**: repairs plus preventive/corrective maintenance merged into one newest-first timeline, optionally narrowed to one asset (404 if the asset doesn't exist). Downtime only ever stated for a *closed* repair (opened → actual return, live data showed a real 6-day downtime); an open repair or a point-in-time maintenance completion leaves the cell empty rather than guessing. Cost shows actual, or estimate marked "(est.)".
- **6 new unit tests** (subtotal/grand-total math, compliance rates incl. the on-time denominator rule, per-row depreciation degradation, merge ordering + downtime, inverted-range rejection, unknown-asset 404). **Full backend suite: 310/310 passing** (304 + 6).

**Frontend**: five new entries in the existing generic Reports picker - a shared optional date-range control for the range-filtered reports, an as-of date for depreciation, nothing else needed; the generic table and CSV download work unchanged (the backbone doing its job). `tsc -b`/`oxlint` clean.

**Click-tested + adversarial against live Postgres**: all five reports returned real data as admin (loss 16 findings with source audits; vendor 14 rows incl. subtotals; compliance 27%/83%/n-a rates over 22 audits; maintenance 17 rows). Loss date-filter from tomorrow → 0 rows; scoped DH's loss report contained only Building-A assets; unauthenticated → 401; COMPLIANCE_OFFICER → 403; inverted range and `asOf=abc` → 400 (the second only correct because of this morning's type-mismatch handler); unknown `assetId` → 404. **Browser-tested as a real Inventory Manager**: all five reports run from the picker and render real content, zero console/network errors, screenshot reviewed.

**Updated status:** EPIC-RPT moves from 6 Built/1 Partial/8 Not-started to **11 Built (01, 02, 03, 04, 05, 06, 07, 08, 09, 10, 14) / 1 Partial (12) / 3 Not started (11, 13, 15)**. Overall: **94 Built / 11 Partial / 75 Not started** (180 total), up from 89/11/80.

**Deliberately not done, and why:** unchanged from the Cluster A entry - Excel/PDF (US-RPT-12's other legs), batch labels (US-RPT-11), scheduled email delivery (US-RPT-13), ad hoc builder (US-RPT-15, Could) - all genuinely infra-shaped, none a small extension of today's work. Vendor-performance metrics beyond spend/quantity totals (e.g. on-time-delivery rates) - no delivery-date-promised field exists anywhere in procurement to compute reliability from; the report presents what the data can actually support.

**Next session:** EPIC-RPT is now 11/15 with every query-shaped story Built; the remaining four are all infra: US-RPT-11 (batch label PDF - the per-asset label pipeline exists), US-RPT-12's Excel/PDF legs (POI/OpenPDF dependencies), US-RPT-13 (scheduler + email - would also unblock EPIC-NTF), US-RPT-15 (Could). Highest-leverage options: an infra session pairing US-RPT-12's Excel/PDF with US-RPT-11's batch labels (both are "render a TabularReport/labels to a binary format" problems), or starting EPIC-NTF/EPIC-SRC as fresh epics, or US-AUD-11's object-storage session (MinIO still provisioned, unused).

---

## 2026-07-15, continued a tenth time — EPIC-SRC started: global search, code lookup, combined filters; 3 Built / 1 Partial / 1 Not started

Picked EPIC-SRC (Search, BR-03, 5 stories) as the fresh-epic option - like DSH and RPT before it, mostly a composition layer over queries prior epics already built, which three sessions in a row have now proven is the cheapest kind of epic to take from zero.

**New `com.iams.search` package (no migration needed - the whole epic rides on existing schema):**

- **US-SRC-01 (`GET /api/v1/search?q=`)**: one term fanned across the entity types the caller may see, grouped. Assets ride the same org-scoped criteria search `GET /assets` uses; people ride `PersonService.list()`'s existing scope filter; **the vendor group is included only when the caller actually holds `inventory:read`** - and the response carries a `vendorsSearched` flag so the UI can distinguish "nothing matched" from "you can't see vendors," rather than teasing a group the caller can't open. Each group capped at 20 (a global search is a preview, not a register). Blank term → 400 before any query runs. Both endpoints deliberately carry no `@PreAuthorize`, the same precedent as `GET /assets`/`GET /persons` (permission-matrix session): everything returned is already reachable through those ungated, org-scoped reads.
- **US-SRC-02 (`GET /api/v1/search/asset-code/{code}`)**: exact-match lookup across every unique identifying code an asset carries - typed asset number, scanned barcode value, QR payload, or RFID tag - in one query (new `findByAnyCodeWithAssociations`, all four columns already uniquely indexed, so AC-SRC-02-H's 1-second resolution is structural). Scanner whitespace trimmed. **An out-of-scope hit is refused (403), not hidden (404)** - the same rule as a direct `GET /assets/{id}`. Unknown code → 404, which the UI turns into AC-SRC-02-X's "register this asset?" affordance for `assets:write` holders only.
- **US-SRC-03 (extends `GET /assets`)**: three new optional filters on the existing endpoint rather than a parallel search API - `orgNodeId` (location subtree, refused if outside the caller's own scope, same rule as the asset-register report), `purchasedFrom`/`purchasedTo` (inclusive, inverted range → 400) - all ANDed with the existing category/status/free-text/scope predicates in `AssetRepositoryImpl`. **AC-SRC-03-X implemented as a sort-field allowlist** (`assetNumber`/`name`/`createdAt`/`purchaseDate`) in `AssetQueryService`: an arbitrary property would otherwise become a Criteria path error deep inside Hibernate (a 500); now it's a 400 naming the supported fields. Verified live: category+location+date-range combined returned exactly the one matching asset; `sort=customAttributes` → 400; `sort=purchaseDate` → 200.
- **US-SRC-05**: `rfidTagId` (on Asset since V11/US-AST-12) added to the free-text OR in `AssetRepositoryImpl` and to the code-lookup columns - searchable from day one, simply never matching until an RFID rollout populates it. The AC's "no error on empty field" falls out of `coalesce`.
- **One near-miss caught before it ran, worth recording as the pattern it is**: the first `SearchController` draft mapped `Person.orgNode.getName()` *in the controller*, after the service transaction closed - `Person.orgNode` is LAZY with no fetch join on its list query, i.e. the exact `LazyInitializationException` class this codebase has hit repeatedly. Caught by inspection against that documented history; mapping moved inside the `@Transactional` service, which now returns plain hit records.
- **8 new unit tests** (`SearchServiceTest`: blank-term rejection before any query, vendor group permission gating both ways, scope-refused code hit, scanner-whitespace trim, unknown-code 404; `AssetQueryServiceTest`: sort allowlist rejection with no repository interaction, inverted purchase-date range). **Full backend suite: 318/318 passing** (310 + 8).

**Frontend**: new `SearchPage` (first nav item, ungated) - one box; an exact `AST-YYYY-NNNNNN` input takes the US-SRC-02 fast path and navigates *straight to the asset detail page* with no results page in between; anything else runs grouped global search. Unknown code renders the not-found alert with "Register this asset" **only** for `assets:write` holders. `tsc -b`/`oxlint` clean.

**Click-tested + adversarial against live Postgres**: global "test" as admin returned both matching assets; code lookup resolved `AST-2026-000002` → Warehouse Test Asset; unknown code → 404, blank/missing `q` → 400, unauthenticated → 401. Viewer's search: `vendorsSearched:false`, zero vendor queries run. IM's search: vendors searched (`medsupply` → both MedSupply vendors; "Acme Supplies" correctly absent - it exists only as PO free-text predating the Vendor entity, verified against `/vendors` rather than assumed a bug). Scoped DH: global search returned only the Building-A asset, and a direct code lookup of an out-of-scope asset → 403. **Browser-tested as IM and Viewer**: code fast path navigated to the asset detail page; unknown code showed the register affordance for IM and correctly withheld it from the Viewer; the vendor group never rendered for the Viewer. Zero unexpected console/network errors (the deliberate unknown-code 404 excluded by design).

**Updated status:** EPIC-SRC moves from 0/0/5 to **3 Built (02, 03, 05) / 1 Partial (01) / 1 Not started (04)**. US-SRC-01 is deliberately Partial, not Built: its AC names "performance targets at 100k assets," and this deployment has four - the free-text legs are unindexed `LIKE` scans that nothing here proves at that scale (a `pg_trgm` GIN index is the known answer if/when a real dataset demands it; the exact-code path is already unique-indexed). Claiming Built on an explicitly scale-qualified AC with a 4-row dataset would be the kind of overstatement this log exists to prevent. US-SRC-04 (saved searches, Should) - a real entity + migration + UI of its own, not force-fit into this session. Overall: **97 Built / 12 Partial / 71 Not started** (180 total), up from 94/11/75.

**Next session:** Options, in rough leverage order: (1) US-SRC-04 (saved searches) plus a `pg_trgm` index to close US-SRC-01 - would take EPIC-SRC to 5/5; (2) the EPIC-RPT infra session (Excel/PDF + batch labels); (3) EPIC-NTF or EPIC-ANL as fresh epics - NTF is the bigger unlock (its email infrastructure also serves US-RPT-13 and several long-deferred notification ACs across SEC/LIF); (4) US-AUD-11 object storage (MinIO provisioned, still unused).
