## 2026-07-16 — EPIC-SRC completed 5/5: saved searches (US-SRC-04) and trigram indexes close US-SRC-01; formal Epic Completion Gate run

Picked up the previous entry's own first option and closed the epic.

**US-SRC-04 (saved searches) - new `SavedSearch` entity, `SavedSearchRepository`, `SavedSearchService`, `SavedSearchController` (migration V41):**

- One row per user-named filter combination over US-SRC-03's asset-search parameters (query/category/status/org-node/purchase-date range), name unique per user **case-insensitively** ("test CAT search" vs "Test cat search" → 409, verified live). **Reference columns deliberately carry no FKs** - the AC requires a saved search referencing a since-deleted category to degrade gracefully at re-apply time, and an FK would either block that deletion or cascade-destroy the saved search; existence is checked at resolve time instead, with the reasoning in both the migration comment and the entity Javadoc.
- `GET /saved-searches/{id}/resolved` is the one-click re-apply: each stored reference existence-checked, dead ones dropped from the effective filter set with a human-readable note, live clauses untouched. **The AC's own scenario executed live, not simulated**: created a throwaway category → saved a search referencing it → deleted the category (204) → resolve returned `categoryId: null`, the query clause intact, and `"Category filter dropped - the saved category no longer exists"`.
- Own-rows-only like `DashboardPreferenceService`: another user's saved-search id is a **404 on list, resolve, and delete** (verified as admin against an IM's row - existence never leaks, and there is no admin path to someone else's searches). Requires ≥1 filter criterion (a name alone → 400); blank name → 400; unauthenticated → 401.
- Frontend on `AssetListPage` (where the filters live): "Save search" button → name dialog; saved searches render as one-click chips with delete; applying a chip whose references died shows the dropped-clause notes as dismissible alerts. Browser-tested end-to-end as `dsh_im`: save → clear → one-click re-apply restored the filter and results; the dead-category chip applied with its note rendered; chip deletion works. Zero console/network errors.

**US-SRC-01 Partial → Built - trigram indexes (same V41):** `pg_trgm` is a *trusted* extension since PG 13, so `CREATE EXTENSION` needs only database-owner privilege - **verified live against this deployment's native PostgreSQL 18 as `iams_app` (which owns the database) before the migration was written**, not assumed. Six GIN indexes over exactly the expressions the criteria queries emit (`lower(name)`, `lower(asset_number)`, `lower(coalesce(serial_number,''))`, `lower(coalesce(rfid_tag_id,''))` on asset; `lower(name)` on vendor; `lower(full_name)` on person). **`EXPLAIN` confirmed the planner serves the search's exact query shape via `idx_asset_name_trgm` (Bitmap Index Scan)** - the structural gap the Partial named is closed. Stated plainly: no 100k-row benchmark was executed (the dataset remains small); what changed is that the known unindexed-scan risk no longer exists, the same structural-satisfaction reasoning US-SRC-02's 1-second AC already used via its unique indexes.

**6 new unit tests** (`SavedSearchServiceTest`: name+filter validation, case-insensitive dup conflict, trimming, cross-user 404, dead-reference notes with live clauses kept, no-notes-when-alive). **Full backend suite: 324/324 passing** (318 + 6). `tsc -b`/`oxlint` clean.

**Epic Completion Gate for EPIC-SRC, run in full:**
- **Epic Review**: BR-03 met end-to-end - one search box across assets/vendors/people (grouped, permission- and scope-filtered), single-step code lookup with the register affordance, combined advanced filters with a sort allowlist, one-click saved searches with graceful degradation, and an RFID field that is searchable today and simply never matches. Every Must and Should story Built; the Could story (US-SRC-05) also Built since it cost one predicate.
- **Adversarial Review (mandatory)**: beyond the prior session's 401/403/400/404 pass - SQL-injection-style name stored inert with the table still queryable; double-delete 204→404 (idempotent refusal); trigram-special characters (`%_'`) in the global search term → 200, no error (JPA parameterization holds for LIKE wildcards - they're treated as literals in the bound value, worst case matching everything, never breaking); **one real find, fixed immediately: a 200-char saved-search name reached the DB's 120-char column and surfaced as a 500** - `@Size` caps mirroring the V41 column widths added to the request DTO, re-verified live as 400. Cross-user access attempts all 404. Scope enforcement re-verified in the prior session (scoped DH: filtered global results, 403 on out-of-scope code hit).
- **Working Software Demonstration**: live walkthrough as real `dsh_im` in the browser (save/re-apply/degrade/delete cycle above) plus the prior session's IM/Viewer phases (code fast path to asset detail, register affordance withheld from Viewer, vendor group permission-gated). Screenshots on file from both sessions.
- **Quality Gates checklist**: All 5 stories Built ✅ · No known Critical/High bugs (the one found this session was fixed and re-verified before this entry) ✅ · 324/324 backend tests, every new service unit-tested ✅ · Build green ✅ · Security: injection/authz/isolation adversarially verified ✅ · Performance: all free-text legs now GIN-indexed, EXPLAIN-verified; exact-code lookups ride unique indexes ✅ · CI pipeline: configured since 2026-07-15, still pending a remote to run against (pre-existing project-wide state, not an SRC gap) ⚠️.
- **Known limitations, stated plainly**: no 100k-row live benchmark (structural readiness only); saved searches store the full US-SRC-03 parameter set but `AssetListPage`'s UI currently exposes only query+category to save (status/location/date-range UI filters remain a small named frontend follow-up); barcode *scanner hardware* flows belong to EPIC-SCN, not this epic.

**Updated status:** EPIC-SRC moves from 3 Built/1 Partial/1 Not-started to **5 Built (01, 02, 03, 04, 05) / 0 / 0 - the third epic completed front-to-back, after CMP and INV (and DSH, whose gate ran inline).** Overall: **99 Built / 11 Partial / 70 Not started** (180 total), up from 97/12/71.

**Deliberately not done, and why:** exposing status/location/date-range as `AssetListPage` UI controls - the backend accepts and saves them; the two filters the page has always had are what a user can currently combine and save, and widening the filter bar is UI polish independent of this epic's ACs (named above as the follow-up it is). A 100k-row synthetic benchmark - fabricating data to prove a number nobody can act on yet adds nothing the EXPLAIN doesn't already show about the mechanism.

**Next session:** unchanged leverage order from before, minus the item just completed: (1) the EPIC-RPT infra session (Excel/PDF export + batch labels - both "render to a binary format" problems, would take RPT to 13-14/15); (2) EPIC-NTF as a fresh epic (email infrastructure unlocks US-RPT-13 plus long-deferred notification ACs across SEC/LIF); (3) US-AUD-11 object storage (MinIO provisioned, still unused); (4) EPIC-ANL (4 stories, smallest untouched epic).

## 2026-07-16, continued — EPIC-PLAT opened with US-PLAT-01: the whole stack ships as one `docker compose up`

Followed the timeline discussion's own recommendation (an installable package early, not last): built US-PLAT-01 (Must, R1, NFR-DEPLOY-01) - the first EPIC-PLAT story - so the product is now deployable by an IT generalist with one command, instead of the run-Maven-and-Vite-by-hand dev workflow being the only way to stand it up.

**What was built:**
- `backend/Dockerfile` - multi-stage: `maven:3.9-eclipse-temurin-21` build (dependency layer warmed separately so source-only rebuilds don't re-download the world) → `eclipse-temurin:21-jre-alpine` runtime as a dedicated non-root user. Tests deliberately run in CI/dev, not the image build.
- `frontend/Dockerfile` - `node:22-alpine` build (Vite 8 needs ≥22.12) → `nginx:stable-alpine` serving the static bundle with an SPA fallback config (`frontend/deploy/nginx.conf`): hashed `/assets/` cached immutable, `index.html` never cached.
- `deploy/proxy/nginx.conf` + a fifth `proxy` service - the stack's single entry point: `/api` and the OpenAPI paths to the backend, everything else to the frontend. The backend has **no host port at all** in the packaged stack; `frontend/src/api/httpClient.ts` already defaulted to a relative `/api/v1` base, so the production bundle needed zero configuration.
- `docker-compose.yml` extended from 2 services (postgres, minio) to the full five, all with real healthchecks and health-gated `depends_on` (postgres → backend → proxy), `restart: unless-stopped`, and every host port overridable (`IAMS_HTTP_PORT`, `DB_HOST_PORT`, `MINIO_API_PORT`, `MINIO_CONSOLE_PORT`) since this very machine demonstrates why (an unrelated `httpd` owns 8080, dev postgres owns 5432).
- `INSTALL.md` - the Installation Guide the AC references: host sizing, the 3-command install, which `.env` values must change before a real deployment, and a troubleshooting section written from the failures actually exercised below (wrong `DB_PASSWORD` against an initialized volume, host-port collisions, reading per-service logs).

**Tested as a genuinely fresh install, not against the dev environment:** a parallel compose project (`-p iams-fresh`, its own new volumes, shifted host ports) - the closest possible simulation of a new host without wiping the dev data. One `docker compose up -d --build` took the stack from nothing to **all five services healthy**: Flyway ran all 41 migrations and seeded the admin on first boot with zero manual post-start steps. Verified through the proxy: admin login 200 on the fresh DB, authed `GET /assets` 200, every SPA deep link 200, `/v3/api-docs` 200, unauthenticated API 401. Browser-tested the real first-run experience with Playwright: login as seeded admin → empty asset register's "Register your first asset" state → created the first category through the UI (a real write through proxy → backend → fresh Postgres) → deep-loaded `/audits` straight through nginx (SPA fallback 200; lands on login by the app's own memory-token design). Screenshots reviewed, zero console/network errors.

**Two real bugs found by the fresh-install test, both fixed and re-verified:**
- **All three HTTP healthchecks failed against `localhost`** - these alpine images resolve `localhost` to `::1` first and nginx's `listen 80` binds IPv4 only, so the frontend sat permanently "unhealthy" while serving perfectly well (and the proxy, correctly, refused to start on top of it - the gating working as designed, on a bad probe). Switched every check to `127.0.0.1`, with the reason as a comment in the compose file.
- **The app's own `/assets` route collided with Vite's `/assets/` build directory**: `try_files $uri $uri/ /index.html` 301-redirected the deep link `/assets` to the *directory* `/assets/` instead of rendering the SPA's asset register. Dropped the `$uri/` directory fallback (an SPA has no meaningful directory URLs) - `/assets` now serves the app, `/assets/index-*.js` still serves the bundle.

**Adversarial pass on the AC's "logs clearly identify the cause" criterion, exercised for real:** recreated the backend with a wrong `DB_PASSWORD` against the initialized volume - Flyway retried, logged `FATAL: password authentication failed for user "iams_app"` seven times, and the container went **unhealthy** in `docker compose ps`; nothing downstream pretended to work (no silent partial-stack state). Restored the password: backend back to healthy, login 200, no data lost. Tried to bind the proxy to a port an existing process owns - compose failed immediately naming the exact port. Both failure modes and their fixes are what INSTALL.md's troubleshooting section documents, because they were observed, not imagined.

**Updated status:** EPIC-PLAT opens at **1 Built (01) / 0 Partial / 15 Not-started**. Overall: **100 Built / 11 Partial / 69 Not started** (180 total), up from 99/11/70.

**Deliberately not done, and why:** adding a docker-image build job to CI - the pipeline is still inert until the repo gets a remote (pre-existing project-wide state); bolting an untestable job onto it adds nothing today. TLS/HTTPS on the proxy - a real R1 concern but its own story (US-PLAT-13 territory), needing cert provisioning decisions the backlog owns. MinIO stays provisioned-but-unused until US-PLAT-02/US-AUD-11 wire object storage into the backend. The `iams-fresh` test project was torn down (`down -v`) after verification; the dev postgres/minio containers were never touched.

**Next session:** (1) US-PLAT-02 + US-AUD-11 as one object-storage session (MinIO SDK, bucket bootstrap, brokered upload/download with checksums - unlocks photo evidence and future attachments in one move, and the packaged stack already ships the store); (2) the EPIC-RPT infra session (Excel/PDF + batch labels); (3) EPIC-NTF (email infra unlocks US-RPT-13 and long-deferred SEC/LIF notification ACs). The packaged deploy also makes every future epic's Working Software Demonstration reproducible on any Docker host - worth keeping green from here on.

## 2026-07-16, continued — US-PLAT-02 (backend-brokered object storage) + US-AUD-11 (photo evidence): MinIO finally consumed, 42 migrations in

Followed the queue laid out for the user earlier today: the object-storage session, because one subsystem unlocks two epics' stories at once. MinIO has been provisioned-but-unused in `docker-compose.yml` since the repo's first compose file; as of this session the backend actually speaks to it.

**New `com.iams.storage` module (US-PLAT-02), the codebase's single object-store path:**
- `Attachment` entity + V42 migration - polymorphic `owner_type`/`owner_id` with no FK (attachments serve audit findings today, asset documents/signatures later; the owning module enforces existence + authorization on every touch), `storage_key` unique, sha256 + size + uploader recorded, rows immutable once written.
- `ObjectStorageClient` - the one class that talks to MinIO (io.minio 8.5.12). Bucket creation is lazy-but-idempotent on first use, deliberately not a startup step: the app must not fail to boot because the object store is momentarily down while nobody is uploading. Any failure surfaces as `StorageUnavailableException` → a real **503** with `STORAGE_UNAVAILABLE` (new handler), not a 500 - verified live by stopping the MinIO container mid-session and watching an upload return exactly that, then succeed again after restart.
- `AttachmentService` - the AC's ordering contract honored literally: content-type allowlist + **magic-byte agreement** (declared `image/png` with executable bytes → 400 "does not match its declared type", proven live) + size cap all checked server-side BEFORE any store write; then object commits FIRST, DB metadata row SECOND. `storeImage()` is deliberately not @Transactional - wrapping external I/O in a DB tx would invert the contract. Hostile filenames get path-stripped (`..\..\secrets\photo.png` → `photo.png`, unit-tested).
- `AttachmentJanitor` - **the codebase's first @Scheduled job** (@EnableScheduling added with a comment explaining why LIF/AUD escalation stays pull-triggered while this doesn't: an orphaned binary has no caller to pull it). Hourly sweep reaps objects older than 24h with no metadata row - the only state the object-first ordering can leak. Survives an unavailable store without crash-looping the scheduler thread (unit-tested).
- Multipart limits raised from Boot's 1MB default to 10MB/12MB in step with `iams.storage.max-size-bytes`; `MaxUploadSizeExceededException` handler added (**413** `UPLOAD_TOO_LARGE`, previously a 500).

**US-AUD-11 on top of it:** `POST/GET /audits/{id}/findings/{findingId}/evidence[/{attachmentId}]` - gated `audits:write`/`audits:read`, anchored on the same `getFinding()` 404-unless-yours discipline as corrections; download is brokered bytes with inline Content-Disposition, **no storage URL ever leaves the backend** (the response DTO deliberately has no key/URL field). No DELETE endpoint exists - evidence follows the module's immutability discipline. Frontend: evidence chips + "Attach photo" per exception-panel finding, fetching bytes through the authed brokered endpoint into an object URL.

**Packaged-stack alignment (keeping yesterday's US-PLAT-01 green):** backend now health-gates on minio and gets `IAMS_STORAGE_ENDPOINT=http://minio:9000`; MinIO's host ports bound to **127.0.0.1 only** (AC: "clients can't reach the object store directly" - network clients now can't; full reverse-proxy isolation incl. postgres is US-PLAT-15's story, named as such in the compose comment). Rebuilt the image and re-ran the whole fresh-install: all five healthy from nothing (42 migrations + admin seed), then the **entire evidence flow executed through the reverse proxy against the fresh stack** - first asset created through the API, audit → damaged finding → upload (sha256 match) → byte-identical download, bucket auto-created on first use with zero manual steps, full adversarial pass repeated. Torn down with `down -v` after; dev containers untouched.

**One real environment bug found by starting the backend, fixed before anything shipped:** V42 originally declared `sha256 CHAR(64)`; Hibernate's `ddl-auto: validate` refuses `bpchar` against a String column (`wrong column type ... found [bpchar], expecting [varchar(64)]`) and the app wouldn't boot. Changed to `VARCHAR(64)` - the migration was created this session and never committed, so editing it (plus resetting the dev DB's V42 row) was legitimate rather than history rewriting. Also confirmed in passing that the *native* PostgreSQL on host 5432 is the dev database, not the compose container that maps the same port - the compose postgres has no flyway history at all.

**9 new unit tests** (AttachmentServiceTest: ordering contract via InOrder, empty/oversized/wrong-type/mismatched-magic-bytes rejections all verified to happen before any store write, hostile-filename sanitization, cross-owner 404; AttachmentJanitorTest: reaps only orphans, survives store outage). **Full suite: 333/333 passing** (324 + 9). `tsc -b`/`oxlint` clean.

**Click-tested live as a real AUDITOR** (fresh `aud11_auditor` user, native backend on 8081 + dev MinIO): create audit → scan MAJOR_DAMAGE finding → upload real PNG (server sha256 == local sha256sum) → list → byte-identical download (`cmp`). Adversarial: unauthenticated 401; IM without `audits:write` 403; nonexistent finding / finding-via-wrong-audit / nonexistent attachment all 404; exe-bytes-as-png 400; declared-pdf 400; 11MB 413; MinIO stopped → 503 with actionable detail. **Browser-tested with Playwright as the auditor**: attach photo through the real file input on the Exceptions panel → chip renders from server state → opens via brokered blob download in a new tab → persists across a fresh login session. Screenshots reviewed, zero console/network errors.

**Updated status:** US-PLAT-02 Built; US-AUD-11 moves Not-started → Built (its offline-capture AC explicitly defers to FR-AUD-19/US-AUD-19, which remains its own Not-started story). EPIC-PLAT: **2 Built / 0 Partial / 14 Not-started**. EPIC-AUD: **17 Built (adds 11) / 3 Partial (03, 15, 17) / 4 Not-started (06, 18, 19, 20)**. Overall: **102 Built / 11 Partial / 67 Not started** (180 total), up from 100/11/69.

**Deliberately not done, and why:** asset-document/signature attachments - the storage module is built generic (`AttachmentOwnerType` extends per consumer) but wiring more owners is those stories' work, not speculative scaffolding today. Evidence capture inside the scan flow itself ("at the moment I record it" - the Exceptions panel covers the recorded finding; a camera affordance inside AuditScanPanel is a small named UX follow-up). Attachment metadata in `AuditFindingResponse` - left out to avoid N+1 storage lookups on every finding serialization; the per-finding evidence endpoint + React Query cache serves the UI cleanly.

**Next session:** per the standing queue: (1) EPIC-RPT binary-export infra - US-RPT-12 Partial→Built (Excel/PDF; pdfbox already a dependency) + US-RPT-11 batch labels, would take RPT to 13/15; (2) EPIC-NTF as the next fresh epic (email infra unlocks US-RPT-13 + long-deferred SEC/LIF notification ACs); (3) EPIC-ANL (4 stories, smallest untouched epic). US-AUD-15's certificate-PDF Partial also rides on (1)'s PDF work.

## 2026-07-16, continued a second time — EPIC-RPT's binary-export infra: US-RPT-12 Partial→Built (Excel/PDF/background jobs), US-RPT-11 Built (batch labels)

The queue's second item. Everything rides on `TabularReport`'s one-shape-for-every-report design decision from the epic's first session - both new exporters and the background path serve all ten reports with zero per-report code.

**US-RPT-12, the two missing formats:**
- `XlsxExporter` (Apache POI 5.3.0, the session's one new dependency) - bold frozen header, auto-sized columns, and **every cell written as text deliberately**: these reports are string-shaped by design, and letting Excel coerce "000123" into a number would corrupt exactly the asset numbers this system exists to keep straight. Verified by ROUND-TRIP in unit tests (file parsed back with POI, cell types asserted), plus a hostile-sheet-title case (Excel's forbidden characters + 31-char cap).
- `PdfExporter` (pdfbox, already on the classpath for labels) - landscape A4, title + row-count stamp, header repeated per page, ellipsis truncation instead of column overflow, WinAnsi sanitization so an unencodable character degrades to `?` instead of killing the render. Round-trip-tested with PDFTextStripper: pagination, first/last row present, header-per-page count.
- `GET /reports/{key}?format=json|csv|xlsx|pdf` - one switch in the existing `render()` helper; unknown format is a 400 naming the options.

**US-RPT-12's background path (the AC's second clause):** `POST /reports/{key}/export-jobs` → 202 + job id, `GET /reports/export-jobs/{id}` (status/progress), `.../download` (409 EXPORT_NOT_READY until COMPLETED, 409 EXPORT_FAILED after a failure - the job's stored error deliberately never leaks internals). Two design points that matter:
- **`DelegatingSecurityContextExecutor`**: report generation applies org-scoping through the caller's security context, which doesn't exist on a worker thread - the wrapper captures it at submit time, so a scoped DH's background export sees exactly what their foreground export would. Without this the async path would have been a scope bypass or a crash.
- `ReportDispatchService` regenerates any report from its key + raw string params by calling the same ReportService methods the typed endpoints call - no duplicated business logic, malformed params are 400s, and an unknown key fails at submit (400) rather than birthing a job doomed to FAIL asynchronously (tightened after the adversarial pass surfaced the uglier 202-then-fail behavior). Jobs are in-memory, own-rows-only (cross-user id → 404), evicted after an hour - stated plainly as single-node-appliance semantics, not pretended distributed infrastructure. The permission split mirrors the typed endpoints: security-events requires `security:read`, the rest `reports:read`, enforced in the @PreAuthorize on submit.

**US-RPT-11 batch labels:** `LabelRenderService.renderBatchPdf()` - one PDF, one page per label at the configured physical size, same composite barcode+QR pipeline as the single label. `BatchLabelService` + `POST /assets/labels/batch`: per the AC, a bad asset is **flagged and excluded, never a failed batch** - "not visible" (missing OR out of org scope, one merged reason so exclusion never leaks which) and "no printable data" both exclude; only a batch where nothing survives is a 400. Exclusions come back in `X-IAMS-Labels-*` headers alongside the PDF. Cap of 500/batch. Frontend: checkbox selection on the asset register (header checkbox with indeterminate state, row clicks still navigate), a "Print n label(s)" action, and an outcome alert that names excluded assets.

**One real bug found live, invisible to every mock-based unit test:** the first mixed batch (2 good + 1 dead id) returned 500 `UnexpectedRollbackException`. `BatchLabelService.render` was `@Transactional(readOnly=true)`, so the per-asset `queryService.get()` calls joined ONE shared transaction - the caught `NotFoundException` still marked it rollback-only, and the commit died even though the code handled the exception correctly. Fixed by dropping the outer transaction (each read runs its own; no cross-asset consistency requirement exists), with the reasoning as a comment on the method. This is precisely the failure class the "catch per item and continue" pattern hits inside a shared tx.

**12 new unit tests** (ExportersTest round-trips, ExportJobServiceTest with a synchronous executor - completion/progress/failure-without-leaking/cross-user-404, BatchLabelServiceTest - mixed exclusions/nothing-survives/size-and-cap validation/dedup). **Full suite: 345/345** (333 + 12). `tsc -b`/`oxlint` clean.

**Click-tested live as the real IM (dsh_im):** xlsx ZIP-magic + pdf %PDF-magic verified on disk; bogus format 400; background job submitted → COMPLETED → downloaded (magic verified); another user's job 404; security-events job as IM 403 / as admin 202; bogus job format 400; mixed batch → 200 PDF with `Rendered: 1, Excluded: 2` headers (one dead id + one asset genuinely outside the IM's scope - the exclusion contract demonstrating itself); all-excluded 400; empty 400; bad size 400; unauthenticated 401. **Browser-tested with Playwright as dsh_im:** ran the report, downloaded real .xlsx via the format picker, ran the background export (progress bar → auto-download), selected 2 assets by checkbox, printed the batch (real PDF download event) and saw the outcome alert. Screenshots reviewed, zero console/network errors.

**Updated status:** US-RPT-12 Partial→Built, US-RPT-11 Not-started→Built. EPIC-RPT: **13 Built / 0 Partial / 2 Not-started (13 scheduled delivery - needs EPIC-NTF's email infra; 15 ad hoc report builder)**. Overall: **104 Built / 10 Partial / 66 Not started** (180 total), up from 102/11/67.

**Deliberately not done, and why:** US-AUD-15's certificate PDF - the PdfExporter is table-shaped; a certificate is a document layout, a small dedicated piece of its own story's work. Persisting export jobs across restarts - contradicts their one-hour download-artifact semantics. Batch-label output as a single page-of-many-stickers sheet layout - the AC says "single print-ready file at the configured size"; page-per-label at exact physical dimensions is what label printers consume.

**Next session:** (1) EPIC-NTF as the next fresh epic - now the single biggest unlock left (email infra completes US-RPT-13, plus long-deferred SEC/LIF notification ACs); (2) EPIC-ANL (4 stories, smallest untouched epic); (3) US-RPT-15 (ad hoc saved reports) or the remaining Partials sweep.

## 2026-07-16, continued a third time — EPIC-NTF built 0/10 to 9 Built / 1 Partial in one session: the notification subsystem exists

The queue's biggest unlock. One new `com.iams.notification` module (V43: notification, preference, versioned template, delivery, trigger-log tables + seeded v1 templates for all 9 catalog events x 2 channels + `notifications:manage` for admins), spring-boot-starter-mail as the session's one new dependency.

**The architecture, in five sentences.** Every producer calls one `NotificationDispatchService.dispatch(event, recipients, vars, resourcePath)` which only WRITES rows - the in-app notification always (US-NTF-03: the channel that cannot fail), plus a PENDING email delivery when the user's preference (or an admin lock) says so - so a slow or down SMTP server can never stall or roll back the business transaction. `NotificationDeliveryJob` (30s) works the delivery queue with exponential backoff and per-attempt logging (US-NTF-08); `NotificationTriggerJob` (hourly) evaluates the US-NTF-06 catalog with an INSERT-first unique-constraint ledger making "exactly once per threshold" true even across overlapping sweeps. Recipients are resolved role x scope AT SEND TIME through the same delegation logic approvals use (US-NTF-07) - no stored recipient list anywhere. Business events reach the module via Spring application events (`TransferDecidedEvent`, `AssetAssignmentChangedEvent`) so lifecycle/asset stay ignorant of notifications - a direct call back would have been a package cycle, since notification already depends on lifecycle for delegation. Rendered text is stored as-sent on both the notification and the delivery, so template edits (immutable version rows, US-NTF-09) never rewrite history.

**Trigger catalog shipped:** upcoming audit at 7/1 days (config), overdue audit repeating every 3 days until closed (threshold key = daysOverdue/repeatDays window), warranty+insurance expiry at 30-day lookahead, maintenance due within 7 days, low stock once per item per day while below reorder, pending approvals (transfers + audits) to the effective approver. All knobs in `NotificationProperties`.

**Live-verified with a real SMTP server** (mailpit, ad hoc container like Playwright - never a committed dependency): overdue-audit sweep fired then fired 0 on immediate re-run (exactly-once proven); 4 real emails landed via actual SMTP with template-rendered subjects; **the full US-NTF-08 retry loop executed live** - stopped mailpit, rejected a transfer, delivery went FAILED/attempt-1/backoff-in-future with `Mail server connection failed` logged, restarted mailpit, forced the retry due, delivery went SENT on attempt 2 and the email arrived. Preference lock 409 (`PREFERENCE_LOCKED`), template v2 saved by admin / 403 for an IM, cross-user notification read 404, bogus event type 400, unauthenticated 401, non-admin sweep 403. Transfer rejection notified the requester with the reason verbatim in the body.

**US-NTF-10 proven in the browser, both legs:** the 401 interceptor now carries `?next=<path>` through login and LoginPage honors it (internal-path-only - absolute URLs ignored, an open-redirect guard), so a logged-out deep link to /settings/notifications landed exactly there after login, not on the homepage. RequireAuth's `from` state (previously captured but ignored by LoginPage - a real pre-existing gap this story closed) works for the client-side bounce. Bell + badge polls 30s, popover marks read + navigates the notification's resourcePath, settings page renders locked types visibly non-editable with a Mandatory chip.

**Two real bugs found by testing, fixed:** (1) TRANSFER_DECISION deep links pointed at `/transfers` - a route that does not exist (transfers live on the asset detail page); found by the browser test's actual click-through, not assumed. Paths corrected to `/assets/{id}` with the event now carrying assetId. (2) The trigger sweep's claim() was originally a self-invoked @Transactional(REQUIRES_NEW) - which silently runs in the caller's transaction; extracted to `TriggerClaimService` so the proxy actually isolates it (the same UnexpectedRollbackException bug class the batch-label service hit this morning, caught in design review this time).

**19 new unit tests** (template render/fail-safe placeholder/versioning; dispatch always-in-app/opt-out/locked-type-override/no-email-skip/dedup; delivery job sent/backoff-math/exhaustion/approval-class-escalation-to-admins/SMS-degrade; query service cross-user-404/idempotent-read/locked-409/defaults). **Full suite: 364/364** (345 + 19). `tsc -b`/`oxlint` clean.

**Updated status:** US-NTF-01/03/04/05/06/07/08/09/10 **Built**; US-NTF-02 (SMS, Could) **Partial** - the `SmsGateway` abstraction + graceful no-gateway degradation are real and tested (AC 2 satisfied live), but no concrete gateway implementation exists to send through and no policy yet creates SMS deliveries, so AC 1 is structurally ready, not done. EPIC-NTF: **9 Built / 1 Partial / 0 Not-started** in its first session. Overall: **113 Built / 11 Partial / 56 Not started** (180 total), up from 104/10/66. Epic Completion Gate deferred until NTF-02 resolves (needs a real gateway decision from the deployment).

**Deliberately not done, and why:** a concrete SMS gateway (no provider exists in this environment to verify against - wiring a fake HTTP gateway would test the mock, not the story); email HTML templating (plain text is template-controlled wording per NTF-09 - markup is presentation scope no AC asks for); notification admin UI for templates (API-complete with permission gating; a template editor screen is UI polish); assignment-event notification of "source/destination approver" (assignments have no approvers in this domain model - transfers do, and their decision events notify requester + both holders; noted as the AC's wording vs. the model's reality). Mailpit was removed after verification; dsh_im keeps the test email address.

**Next session:** (1) US-RPT-13 (scheduled report delivery) - now unlocked by this session's email infra, would take EPIC-RPT to 14/15; (2) EPIC-ANL (4 stories, smallest untouched epic); (3) the Partials sweep (11 stories, several now cheap: AUD-15's certificate PDF rides on PdfExporter, NTF-02 needs a gateway decision).

## 2026-07-16, continued a fourth time — Working Software Demo published; one real health-probe bug found by demoing

Ran the demo the user asked for as a live walkthrough, not a slide deck: 8 flows captured from the running application as real scoped users (dashboard, asset register with batch-label selection, asset lifecycle detail, audit with photo evidence, reports with export formats, inventory, notification bell + settings, global search) and published as a self-contained demo page with embedded screenshots.

**A real bug surfaced by the demo itself:** with the dev SMTP catcher removed after the NTF session, `/actuator/health` returned **503** - spring-boot-starter-mail auto-registers a MailHealthIndicator, so any SMTP outage marked the whole appliance unhealthy, directly contradicting EPIC-NTF's own design (email failures retry with backoff; in-app notifications are unaffected). In the packaged stack this would have flipped the backend container unhealthy - and blocked the proxy - the moment a mail relay hiccuped. Fixed with `management.health.mail.enabled: false` and the reasoning as a comment. This is exactly why demos run against the real thing.

**Status:** no story-tier change. Overall unchanged at **113 Built / 11 Partial / 56 Not started** (180 total).

**Next session:** unchanged queue - (1) US-RPT-13 scheduled report delivery (email infra now exists), (2) EPIC-ANL, (3) the Partials sweep.

## 2026-07-16, continued a sixth time — US-RPT-13 Built: scheduled report delivery, EPIC-RPT reaches 14/15

The story EPIC-NTF unlocked this morning. New `report_schedule` table (V44) + `ReportScheduleService` (create/list/delete, own-rows-only like saved searches and export jobs, validation at creation: known report key, csv/xlsx/pdf, 1-10 syntactically valid recipient emails) + `ReportScheduleJob` (5-minute sweep + an admin run-due endpoint for deterministic testing/ops).

**The design decision that matters: each due schedule runs UNDER ITS OWNER'S IDENTITY.** A `CurrentUser` is reconstructed from the owner's live roles/permissions and set on the security context for exactly the duration of the run (restored in `finally`), so a scoped Department Head's standing report contains what their own foreground run would - never more. Same scope-safety reasoning as the export-job path's DelegatingSecurityContextExecutor, extended to runs that outlive any request. Because roles/permissions/scope are re-read from the DB at run time, a role change or scope change applies to the very next delivery - no stale grants.

**AC 1 executed live, not simulated** (mailpit): monthly xlsx schedule to 3 recipients → forced due → run → **one email, all three addresses, a real `asset-register-2026-07-16.xlsx` attachment** with the correct OOXML content type; `lastOutcome` records "Delivered to 3 recipient(s)" and `nextRunAt` advanced a month. **AC 2 executed live too**: created a throwaway owner, deactivated them (via the real versioned deactivate endpoint), forced their weekly schedule due → status flipped to `PAUSED_OWNER_DEACTIVATED` with "paused for reassignment" recorded, **and an in-app admin alert raised** (unread count observed incrementing) - flagged, not silently failing forever. A failing run records `Failed: <cause>` and still advances to the next period rather than hammering every sweep (unit-tested).

`EmailSender` gained `sendWithAttachment` (MimeMessageHelper) - the first non-plain-text mail in the codebase. Frontend: a "Schedule…" dialog on the Reports page (frequency, comma-separated recipients, uses the page's current filters and format picker) and a "My scheduled reports" panel showing recipients, next run, last outcome, a paused-owner warning chip, and delete.

**Adversarial:** delete someone else's schedule 404 (existence never leaks); bad email/format/report-key 400; security-events schedule without `security:read` 403 (same permission split as the typed endpoints and export jobs); run-due without `notifications:manage` 403; unauthenticated 401. **7 new unit tests** (service validation/ownership/frequency math; job delivery-to-all/pause-and-flag/fail-and-advance + context cleanup assertion). **Full suite: 371/371.** `tsc -b`/`oxlint` clean; browser-tested the dialog → list → delete loop as dsh_im (the only console noise was Vite's dev-cache "Outdated Optimize Dep" 504, a dev-server artifact, not an app error).

**Updated status:** US-RPT-13 Not-started → **Built**. EPIC-RPT: **14 Built / 0 Partial / 1 Not-started (15, the ad hoc report builder)**. Overall: **114 Built / 11 Partial / 55 Not started** (180 total), up from 113/11/56.

**Deliberately not done, and why:** schedule reassignment UI (the pause flags it for an admin; transferring ownership is a small follow-up nobody's AC demands yet); cron-precision timing (DAILY/WEEKLY/MONTHLY intervals satisfy the AC's "monthly" wording; a time-of-day picker is polish); MONTHLY is 30 days, stated plainly rather than calendar-month arithmetic pretending to a precision the AC doesn't ask for. The throwaway rpt13_owner stays deactivated with its paused schedule - it is itself a standing demonstration of the reassignment flag.

**Next session:** (1) EPIC-ANL (4 stories, last small untouched epic); (2) US-RPT-15 (ad hoc report builder - would complete EPIC-RPT and earn its gate); (3) Partials sweep; (4) Dependabot triage (18 PRs, majors are real migrations).

## 2026-07-17 — EPIC-ANL built 0/4 to 4 Built in one session: deployment-local product analytics, and the epic completes with its gate

The queue's next item, and the last small untouched epic. One new `com.iams.analytics` module (V45: append-only `usage_event` + `feedback_item` tables, seeded FEEDBACK_RECEIVED templates riding on EPIC-NTF's catalog). Zero new dependencies.

**US-ANL-01, server-side usage capture.** A `@TrackUsage(module, action)` annotation on ~20 curated controller methods (report runs, asset register/list, audit create/scan/submit, label prints, inventory list/adjust, search, dashboard view, feedback submit) and a `UsageTrackingInterceptor` (the codebase's first HandlerInterceptor/WebMvcConfigurer) that records in `afterCompletion` — only 2xx completions by an authenticated CurrentUser. The ordering IS the second AC: by the time capture runs the response is already committed, so "analytics never blocks a user-facing operation" is structural, and `UsageRecorder` additionally swallows every failure into a WARN (unit-tested with a throwing repository). One row per role held at action time — "module, action, role" stays flat and exactly aggregatable for multi-role users, and the report legitimately counts them toward both roles. No client-side tracking script exists anywhere.

**US-ANL-03, the adoption report.** `AdoptionReportService` produces a `TabularReport` (key `usage-adoption`) so the entire EPIC-RPT surface — csv/xlsx/pdf, background export jobs, scheduled email delivery — works on it with zero new export code. The matrix is EXPECTATION-driven, not observation-driven: expected role×module cells derive from each role's own permission grants (wildcard roles expected everywhere; `search` expected of everyone; custom roles land in the right cells automatically), and an expected-but-unused cell renders as a flagged `GAP (expected, no usage)` row — the AC's "visible, not averaged away" — with `NEAR-ZERO` below 5 events and observed-only rows (e.g. `feedback`) shown unflagged. Only roles somebody currently holds appear. Gated on a new `analytics:read` permission deliberately seeded to NO role: only the Super Administrator's wildcard (or a future deliberate grant) passes. The per-key permission split (security-events→security:read, usage-adoption→analytics:read, rest→reports:read) moved out of two duplicated @PreAuthorize SpEL ternaries into one `ReportAccessPolicy` bean both key-parameterized endpoints share.

**US-ANL-04, in-app feedback.** `POST /feedback` open to every authenticated user (the persona is Employee/Volunteer, the least-privileged role): category enum + optional text (blank collapses to null — category alone accepted per the AC) + the submitting page path as context. The item persists as the durable record; a `FeedbackSubmittedEvent` (analytics module) is handled by `NotificationEventListeners` (notification→analytics, never the reverse — same dependency direction reasoning as the lifecycle events) and dispatched as FEEDBACK_RECEIVED to holders of the configured recipient role (`iams.notifications.feedback-recipient-role`, default ADMIN, falling back to admins if nobody holds it) with the full content in the rendered body. The 201 receipt + UI snackbar is the confirmation leg. Frontend: a feedback icon in the app bar for every role, dialog with category picker + optional text.

**US-ANL-02, sovereignty as structure, not policy.** (1) The analytics module's only inbound API is user-authored feedback — there is deliberately no endpoint through which a client can submit usage events, and nothing in the module's code path can make an outbound network call. Both facts are now enforced by `AnalyticsSovereigntyTest`, which scans the module's actual sources for every outbound-capable client on the classpath and for write-endpoints outside FeedbackController — a future edit that adds either fails the BUILD, not a review. (2) The US-CMP-05 data-residency view now NAMES each store (PostgreSQL incl. usage-analytics and feedback data; MinIO) with an on-premises flag, rendered as a "Data Stores" list on the Compliance page — the AC's "confirmed on-premises alongside every other store" is a readable line, not an inference.

**26 new unit tests** (recorder: row-per-role/NONE-role/never-throws; interceptor: 2xx-only/exception/unannotated/unauthenticated/recorder-failure-never-propagates; adoption: GAP visibility/near-zero/OK/omission/wildcard/unheld-role/non-catalog-module/period validation; feedback service: trim+publish/category-only/missing-category/oversize; listeners: configured-role routing/admin fallback/no-text marker; sovereignty: both structural scans). **Full suite: 397/397** (371 + 26). `tsc -b`/`oxlint` clean. One test-authoring stumble caught by the first run: the role() helper stubbed a mock inside `when(findAll()).thenReturn(...)` — Mockito's nested-stubbing error; roles now built before stubbing.

**Click-tested live** (fresh `anl_emp` EMPLOYEE_VOLUNTEER + `anl_im` INVENTORY_MANAGER, native backend on 8081, V45 applied on boot): tracked actions as both users, then the adoption report as admin showed exactly the truth — INVENTORY_MANAGER NEAR-ZERO on assets/inventory/reports/search with a dashboard GAP, EMPLOYEE_VOLUNTEER's feedback module as an observed-only row, every idle role a wall of GAP rows — and a second run showed the admin's own first run captured (`SUPER_ADMIN | reports | 1`), server-side capture proving itself. Feedback routing verified in the DB: both submissions notified BOTH holders of the ADMIN role (jsmith, adminuser2 — from prior sessions), correctly NOT the SUPER_ADMIN dev admin, because the configured recipient role is ADMIN — the config working as designed, checked rather than assumed. **Adversarial:** unauthenticated feedback/adoption 401; IM and Employee adoption 403; IM adoption export-job 403 and schedule 403 (ReportAccessPolicy enforcing on both key-parameterized paths); bogus/missing category 400; 2500-char message 400; withinDays 0/9999 400; bogus format 400; xlsx magic `504b`; background pdf job 202→COMPLETED→`%PDF`.

**Browser-tested with Playwright as the real Employee/Volunteer** (the story's persona): feedback dialog from the app bar → category + text → snackbar receipt; Reports nav correctly absent for the employee; the report picker as IM correctly does NOT offer Feature Adoption; as admin the Feature Adoption report renders with GAP rows and the Compliance page shows the Data Stores list. Zero console errors, zero failed requests, screenshots reviewed.

**Epic Completion Gate (EPIC-ANL): PASSED.** BR-20/BO-5 objective met — usage analytics and feedback exist, are useful (the gap matrix is actionable training/UX signal), and cannot leave the deployment by construction, with the guarantee executable in CI. Adversarial pass done above; accessibility: the new dialog/button are label/role-addressable (the Playwright selectors are the proof). Known limitations, stated: the tracked catalog is curated, not exhaustive (extending = one annotation); NEAR-ZERO is a fixed threshold of 5 events, not statistical; feedback has no triage UI (the routed notification carries the full content; the table is the durable record) — none of these are AC gaps.

**Deliberately not done, and why:** a feedback triage/inbox screen (no AC asks for it; the notification body carries everything); usage-event retention policy hookup (EPIC-CMP's retention engine targets business entities — adding `usage_event` is a one-line RetentionEntityType follow-up if the Compliance Officer ever asks); tracking every endpoint (the catalog rule exists precisely to avoid recording six events per page load). Dev convenience shipped alongside: the Vite proxy target is now `IAMS_API_TARGET`-overridable (dev backends here run on 8081 since httpd squats 8080). Test users anl_emp/anl_im kept — their captured events are the adoption report's standing demonstration data.

**Updated status:** US-ANL-01/02/03/04 all Not-started → **Built**. EPIC-ANL: **4 Built / 0 Partial / 0 Not-started — COMPLETE with gate.** Overall: **118 Built / 11 Partial / 51 Not started** (180 total), up from 114/11/55.

**Next session:** (1) US-RPT-15 (ad hoc report builder — would complete EPIC-RPT and earn its gate); (2) the Partials sweep (11 stories; AUD-15's certificate PDF rides on PdfExporter, NTF-02 needs a gateway decision); (3) Dependabot triage (18 PRs, majors are real migrations); (4) or open one of the remaining untouched epics (MIG/SCN/INT; PLAT has 14 Not-started enablers that pair well with whichever epic needs them).

## 2026-07-18 — US-RPT-15 Built: the ad hoc report builder; EPIC-RPT completes 15/15 with its gate

The queue's next item. An unusual session start: the working tree already held a complete, uncommitted US-RPT-15 implementation (service, entity, repository, V46, 9 unit tests, frontend panel) from a prior session that evidently ended before verifying or logging it. Rather than assuming it worked, it was reviewed line-by-line against the ACs and this codebase's conventions, then taken through the full battery as if freshly written — which is the point of the discipline: nothing here was taken on faith from a session that couldn't vouch for it.

**What US-RPT-15 is, as implemented.** `AdHocReport` (V46, `adhoc_report`): an ordered field selection plus the standard asset filter set (text query, category, status, org node, purchase-date range), own-rows-only exactly like `SavedSearch`/export jobs — `findByIdAndUserId`, so another user's report id is a 404 and existence never leaks, *including from the SUPER_ADMIN wildcard* (verified live: admin got 404 on an IM's report for both run and delete). The field catalog is server-defined — 18 built-in asset fields plus every CURRENT `AssetCustomFieldDefinition` (distinct by fieldKey, labeled "(custom)") — so "available fields" is always what the schema actually offers. Save-time strictness (unknown field → 400 naming it; ≤30 fields; per-user case-insensitive name uniqueness backed by DB constraint `uq_adhoc_report_user_name`), run-time leniency (the AC): a field whose definition was removed after saving is omitted with a note appended to the report title; a filter whose referenced entity died is dropped with a note — the `SavedSearchService.resolve()` discipline, never a hard failure. Rows come from the same org-scoped `assetRepository.search` the asset register uses, so an ad hoc report can never out-see its owner. Reference columns carry NO FKs (same V41 reasoning): degradation is checked at run time, never enforced against future deletions. Runs render through the existing `render()` helper, so json/csv/xlsx/pdf all work with zero new export code. Five endpoints under `/reports/ad-hoc`, all on `reports:read` — building a personal report grants nothing the register doesn't already show. Frontend: `AdHocReportsPanel` on the Reports page (builder dialog with checkbox palette + filter pickers, all queries `enabled`-gated on dialog open per the standing discipline; saved list with run/download/delete; results render through the page's existing table, so the degradation note in the title is user-visible).

**Verification (all this session):** 9 unit tests reviewed and re-run — save-time validation, run-time column order + custom values + bulk person resolution, removed-field omission with note, dead-category-filter drop reaching the search as null, foreign-id 404, catalog dedup. **Full suite: 406/406** (397 + 9). `tsc -b`/`oxlint` clean. **Click-tested live 30/30** (native Postgres, backend on 8081, V46 applied on boot, fresh `rpt15_im_*` INVENTORY_MANAGER + `rpt15_emp_*` EMPLOYEE_VOLUNTEER): field catalog offers built-ins + a just-created custom field; create 201 → appears in own list → run returns the exact saved column order with the custom value; **rerun-with-current-data AC proven** (admin added an asset, IM's rerun went 1→2 rows); csv/xlsx (`504b`)/pdf (`%PDF`) all real bytes; **degradation AC proven live** (removed the custom field definition via category PATCH, rerun → 200, column omitted, title = "… — Column 'rpt15Cover' omitted - the field no longer exists", rows intact). **Adversarial:** anon 401; employee 403 on list and create; admin 404 on foreign run/delete; 400 on empty fields, unknown field, >30 fields, inverted date range, bogus format; 409 on case-insensitive duplicate name; injection-style name stored inert; nonexistent id 404. **Browser-tested with Playwright as the real Inventory Manager persona:** login → Reports → built "IM browser-built report" in the dialog (5 fields), saved, ran it — results table rendered 6 rows with the right columns — deleted it from the list (delete verified via API; the Playwright waiter itself was ambiguous because the results header legitimately keeps the report name on screen). Zero console errors, zero failed network requests, screenshots reviewed.

**Epic Completion Gate (EPIC-RPT): PASSED — the epic is 15/15 Built.** BR-10 objective met end-to-end: eleven standard reports (register, department/room, employee assets, missing/lost/damaged, expiry, purchase/vendor, movements, audit compliance, depreciation, maintenance, security events) + batch labels + universal PDF/Excel/CSV export with background jobs for large runs + scheduled email delivery + the ad hoc builder, every one driven through a real browser or the live API at some point across the epic's four sessions. **Gate adversarial pass, this session's additions:** same-name double-submit race → exactly one 201, one 409, one row persisted (the DB unique constraint arbitrating, not just the pre-check); regression smoke across the whole report surface after the controller change (catalog report 200, csv 200, background job 202→COMPLETED→`%PDF-1.6`, schedules list 200); and confirmed the keyed endpoints reject `ad-hoc` as a report key (400 on `/reports/ad-hoc/export-jobs` and `/reports/ad-hoc/schedules`) — no accidental crossover between the catalog infrastructure and personal definitions. Accessibility: every builder control is label/role-addressable (the Playwright selectors — `getByLabel`, `getByRole('checkbox', name)`, aria-labeled icon buttons — are the proof). **Known limitations, stated plainly:** the ad hoc field catalog covers the asset-register domain only (assets + custom fields), not inventory/audit/lifecycle entities — the AC's persona and "available fields" language is asset-analytical and no AC asks for more; ad hoc reports are deliberately NOT schedulable or background-exportable (that infra is catalog-keyed; the AC asks for on-demand rerun, which is what exists); the dead-filter degradation legs (category/status/location) are unit-tested while the removed-field leg is additionally proven live; one earlier gate finding stands unchanged — scheduled-delivery email requires the compose mail container when running the full stack.

**Deliberately not done, and why:** extending the builder to non-asset domains (no AC; would need a per-domain field catalog + permission mapping — real scope, not a gap in this story); wiring ad hoc definitions into US-RPT-13 schedules (the AC's "reruns on demand" is exactly what's built; schedules are catalog-keyed by design). Test users `rpt15_im_115831`/`rpt15_emp_115831`, the temp category, its two assets, and the "Temp category snapshot" definition (with its degraded custom-field column) are kept as standing demonstration data — the saved report now permanently demonstrates the degradation note live.

**Updated status:** US-RPT-15 Not-started → **Built**. EPIC-RPT: **15 Built / 0 Partial / 0 Not-started — COMPLETE with gate.** Overall: **119 Built / 11 Partial / 50 Not started** (180 total), up from 118/11/51.

**Next session:** (1) the Partials sweep — 11 stories, several cheap: AUD-15's certificate PDF rides on the now-proven PdfExporter, NTF-02 needs a gateway decision first; (2) Dependabot triage (18 PRs; majors are real migrations, minors are probably batchable); (3) or open one of the three remaining untouched epics (MIG/SCN/INT — INT-03 LDAP/SSO is the only R1 Must among them; PLAT's 14 Not-started enablers pair well with whichever is chosen).

## 2026-07-18, continued — US-AUD-15 Partial→Built: the audit completion certificate as a formal, downloadable PDF

First item off the Partials sweep, and the one the queue had flagged as cheap-because-the-PdfExporter-exists. It turned out the certificate wanted its own renderer, not the exporter — which is exactly why it had been deferred as "a small dedicated piece of its own story's work" rather than bolted onto the table exporter.

**What was already there vs. what closed the Partial.** The certificate *data* (counts, approver id, approved-at) and the closed-only gate were already Built and tested — the summary already rendered in the audit workflow panel. The AC's actual words are "a completion certificate … is generated and **downloadable**," and downloadable-as-a-formal-record is what was missing: there was no document artifact, only an on-screen summary. That's the gap this closes.

**New `AuditCertificatePdfRenderer`** — deliberately NOT `PdfExporter`. The exporter is table-shaped (landscape grid, repeated header row, one row per record); a certificate is a document layout: centered title, a statement naming the audit, a summary block (assets in scope / verified / missing / damaged), and the approver + date, with a footer carrying the generation timestamp and the audit reference UUID. Same pdfbox Standard-14 constraints as the exporter (WinAnsi-only; unencodable characters replaced, never a mid-render throw — unit-tested with a CJK audit name that renders as `?`). The certificate endpoint gained a `?format=` param (`json` default for the in-app summary, `pdf` for the download) sharing ONE `reportService.certificate()` call, so the closed-only gate and the counts can never disagree between formats — proven live: the 409 fires on both `json` and `pdf` for a non-closed audit. The service now also resolves the approver's UUID to a display name, **leniently** — a since-deleted approver account resolves to null, never making a historical certificate unretrievable (dedicated unit test). `AuditCertificateResponse` gained `approverName`.

**Frontend:** the workflow panel's existing "Completion Certificate" block gained an "Approved by {name} on {date}" line and a "Download certificate (PDF)" button (blob download, same pattern as batch labels). No new page — this rides on the audit detail already built for EPIC-AUD.

**Verification (all this session):** 2 new renderer tests (PDF text extracted with pdfbox and asserted to contain the title/audit-name/counts/approver/date/reference; the missing-approver + unencodable-character path) + 1 updated service test (approver-name resolution) + 1 new (approver account deleted → certificate still retrievable, name null). **Full suite: 409/409** (406 + 3). `tsc -b`/`oxlint` clean. **Click-tested live 16/16** (native Postgres, backend on 8081, fresh `aud15_dh_*` DEPARTMENT_HEAD approver + `aud15_emp_*` no-audits-read user): drove a real audit create → submit (admin re-auth, the one unscanned expected asset auto-classified Missing) → **admin self-approve correctly blocked 403 (US-AUD-22)** → DH approve → CLOSED; then certificate json names the approver ("Dana Head", expected 1 / missing 1), certificate pdf returns `%PDF` bytes as an `attachment` with `application/pdf` content-type, DH can download it too. **Adversarial:** non-closed 409 (both formats), anon 401, no-audits-read user 403, bogus format 400, nonexistent audit 404. **Browser-tested with Playwright as the real DEPARTMENT_HEAD persona** (not admin — the approver is who actually wants the certificate): logged in, navigated to the closed audit, saw "Approved by Dana Head on 18/07/2026" and the download button, clicked it → download fired (`audit-certificate-….pdf`), intercepted the request at `status=200 type=application/pdf`. Zero console errors, zero failed network requests, screenshot reviewed (the panel shows the counts, the approver line, and the button exactly as designed).

**Deliberately not done, and why:** embedding a scanned/e-signature image on the certificate (no AC asks for it; the re-auth signature at submit — US-AUD-13 — is the legal attestation, and the approver is named on the certificate); a certificate for audits closed before this renderer existed renders identically on demand (the data was always there — nothing to backfill). The other two EPIC-AUD Partials (03 continuous-scan UX, 17 dashboard "recent/closed" section) are untouched — separate scope, not this story.

**Updated status:** US-AUD-15 Partial → **Built**. EPIC-AUD moves from 17 Built / 3 Partial (03, 15, 17) / 4 Not-started to **18 Built / 2 Partial (03, 17) / 4 Not-started (06, 18, 19, 20)**. Overall: **120 Built / 10 Partial / 50 Not started** (180 total), up from 119/11/50.

**Next session:** continue the Partials sweep — the cheapest remaining are likely AUD-17's dashboard "recent/closed" section (the dashboard query already exists, it's a filter + a UI section) and the SEC/USR session-token Partials; NTF-02 (SMS) still needs a real gateway decision before it can move. Then Dependabot triage (18 PRs) or a fresh epic (MIG/SCN/INT).

## 2026-07-18, continued a second time — US-AUD-17 Partial→Built: the audit dashboard now shows recent audits + exceptions + pending-approval, closing its last two AC gaps

Second Partials-sweep item, and — as the prior entry predicted — a cheap one: the query infrastructure already existed, this was a filter plus a UI section plus surfacing a count that was already being computed and then thrown away.

**The two precise gaps against US-AUD-17's AC** ("a dashboard showing in-progress **and recent** audits … progress %, **exceptions**, and pending approvals are visible"): (1) the dashboard showed only in-progress audits — `AuditReportService.dashboard()` filtered out CLOSED, so there was no "recent" half; (2) the DSH audit-completion tile mapped away the `exceptionCount` that `AuditReportService.dashboard()` already computed per audit, so exceptions were invisible. Pending-approval was technically present (the status string) but not called out. Empty state already existed. Nothing else in the AC was missing.

**Backend.** `AuditReportService` gained `recentlyClosed(int limit)` — closed audits in the caller's scope (reusing the already-scope-filtered `auditService.list(CLOSED)`), sorted by `approvedAt` newest-first (null approvedAt sorts last via `nullsLast`, never throws), capped; the per-audit item build (progress + exception count) was extracted into a shared `toDashboardItem` so active and recent rows are identical in shape. `DashboardService.auditCompletion()` now carries `exceptionCount` on each item and a `recentlyClosed` list; **the average stays computed over ACTIVE audits only** — a pile of 100%-complete closed audits must not flatter "how are the audits I still have to finish doing." `AuditCompletionItemResponse` gained `exceptionCount`; `AuditCompletionResponse` gained `recentlyClosed`. No new endpoint, no migration, no new permission (the tile is already `dashboards:read`, which DEPARTMENT_HEAD — the AC persona — holds since V39).

**Frontend.** The existing "Audit Completion" dashboard tile: each active audit now shows a "Pending approval" chip when `PENDING_APPROVAL` and a red "N exceptions" chip when it has any; a new "Recently closed" divider section lists the recent closed audits (exception counts + a green "Closed" chip); the empty state now fires only when there are neither active nor recent audits (previously it hinged on the active-average being null, which would have hidden a dashboard that had only recent audits).

**Verification (all this session):** 2 new backend tests (service: exception counts surfaced + recentlyClosed section + average-excludes-closed; report service: `recentlyClosed` newest-first ordering with null-approvedAt handling and the limit) + the 2 existing DSH audit-completion tests updated for the new record shape. **Full suite: 411/411** (409 + 2). `tsc -b`/`oxlint` clean. **Click-tested live 16/16** (native Postgres, backend on 8081, fresh AUDITOR user reusing the AUD-15 DEPARTMENT_HEAD): drove create → submit (audit shows in ACTIVE with `PENDING_APPROVAL` and `exceptionCount ≥ 1` from the auto-Missing asset) → approve → CLOSED (audit leaves ACTIVE, appears in `recentlyClosed` **with its exception count preserved**, sorts first, section capped at 5). **Adversarial:** anon 401, no-`dashboards:read` user 403. **Browser-tested with Playwright as the real DEPARTMENT_HEAD persona:** dashboard rendered with the "Pending approval" chip, red exception chips, and the "Recently closed" section all visible; zero console errors, zero failed requests, screenshot reviewed (five recently-closed audits with exception counts + green Closed chips below the six active audits).

**Deliberately not done, and why:** a dedicated standalone audit-dashboard *page* (the shared DSH tile IS the home US-AUD-17 was always intended to land in — the log said so when EPIC-DSH was built; a second page would duplicate it); cross-cycle trend analytics (that's US-AUD-18, a separate Not-started story, explicitly out of scope here); making the recent-closed limit configurable (5 is a sensible dashboard default; no AC asks for a control).

**Updated status:** US-AUD-17 Partial → **Built**. EPIC-AUD: **19 Built / 1 Partial (03 — category/asset-scoped audits pass org-scope filtering unrestricted, a documented gap) / 4 Not-started (06, 18, 19, 20)**, up from 18/2/4. Overall: **121 Built / 9 Partial / 50 Not started** (180 total), up from 120/10/50.

**Next session:** the Partials sweep continues — remaining are AUD-03 (org-scope filtering for category/asset-scoped audits, a real design question, not a quick win), SEC/USR session-token Partials, LIF-04/13, and NTF-02 (still needs a gateway decision). Then Dependabot triage (18 PRs) or a fresh epic (MIG/SCN/INT).

## 2026-07-18, continued a third time — US-LIF-04 Partial→Built (department custodianship); a pre-existing app-wide optimistic-lock 401 bug found and fixed while testing it

Third Partials-sweep item, and a genuine "prerequisite unblocked by a later epic" case - exactly what the standing convention says to re-check each session. US-LIF-04's department half was deferred (2026-07-13) because "Asset carries no department reference and Department isn't wired into Asset/Person yet." Re-checking this session: the `Department` entity (FR-ORG-03) now exists as a standalone dimension with full CRUD. The blocker is gone, so the half that was Partial is now buildable.

**Custodian is a Person XOR a Department.** New nullable `asset.assigned_to_department_id` (V47, FK to department). `AssetAssignmentService` is the single writer of both columns and keeps them mutually exclusive: assigning either kind clears the other, so a person→department (or the reverse) switch is ONE `ASSIGNMENT_CHANGE` row whose old/new labels cross the kind boundary - that IS the AC's "prior assignment explicitly closed, not silently overwritten," now applied across both custodian kinds. History moved from the raw `assignedToPersonId` column name to a unified `"custodian"` field, because that reads correctly whichever kind is involved (browser-confirmed: the timeline shows `custodian: Facilities 304560 (CC-304560) → Custodian 304560`, a clean cross-kind row). New `POST /assets/{id}/assignment/department`; `AssetResponse`/mapper expose `assignedToDepartmentId`. **No `AssetAssignmentChangedEvent` on the department path** - US-NTF-04 notifies the assigned *person*, and a department is not a notifiable recipient; there is no person to notify. The person path's notification is unchanged. Frontend: the assignment panel gained a Person/Department toggle and a department autocomplete (departments fetched only while the picker is open, the enabled-gating discipline); the current-custodian display names the kind; a new minimal `departmentApi` client (list is open to any authenticated user, like persons).

**Bug found while running the adversarial pass, and fixed (pre-existing, app-wide):** the stale-version case returned **401 "Unauthenticated" instead of 409** - and not just on my new endpoint. Root cause (from the server log): `ApiExceptionHandler.handleOptimisticLockConflict` put the raw JPA entity into the ProblemDetail as `currentResource`; serializing an entity with an uninitialized LAZY association (here `Asset → OrgNode → OrgLevel`) throws `LazyInitializationException` AFTER the handler returns, during response writing, which cascades to a servlet `/error` dispatch that runs the security filter with no SecurityContext and returns 401. This affected **every** optimistic-lock conflict on an entity with lazy proxies across all ~24 call sites (proven live: asset PATCH, asset status, and the untouched person-assignment path all 401'd identically) - so `currentResource` was already undeliverable for assets and the frontend's `ConflictDialog` had never actually received it (it degrades gracefully to "—"). The only frontend consumer of `currentResource` is the asset-edit dialog, and there it was already non-functional. Fix: the handler no longer embeds the raw entity - it keeps the actionable scalars (`expectedVersion`, `currentVersion`). One line, zero regression, and it converts a misleading 401 into a correct 409 app-wide (and makes the asset-edit conflict dialog reachable for the first time, since it keys on `errorCode === 'OPTIMISTIC_LOCK_CONFLICT'`, which it never saw before). A full server-side snapshot in the conflict body (API §5.1) would need a resource-specific DTO mapping and is left as its own follow-up rather than bolted on here. This is the exact "fix real, connected gaps found while building, immediately" the charter calls for - found by testing my own endpoint, fixed in the same session, not deferred.

**Verification (all this session):** 5 new/updated `AssetAssignmentServiceTest` cases (department assign records history + publishes NO event; inactive department 409; person→department and department→person each close the prior custodian in one row; unassign from a department publishes no event) plus the three existing person tests updated to the unified `"custodian"` field. **Full suite: 416/416** (411 + 5), re-run green after the exception-handler fix too. `tsc -b`/`oxlint` clean. **Click-tested live 16/16** (native Postgres, backend on 8081, V47 applied on boot): assign→department (person null), unified `custodian` history label, switch to person (department cleared, one row old=dept new=person), switch to a second department (person cleared), unassign (both null); **adversarial:** inactive department 409, stale version now **409** (the fixed path), nonexistent department 404, missing departmentId 400, anon 401, no-`assets:write` user 403. **Browser-tested with Playwright as INVENTORY_MANAGER** (the AC persona): opened an asset, toggled the picker to Department, assigned "Facilities 304560 (CC-304560)" - the custodian shows with its "Department" kind label and the History timeline renders every cross-kind transition under the `custodian` field. Two console 404s (`/insurance`, `/depreciation-override`) are pre-existing optional-sub-resource fetches that 404 for any asset lacking those details (confirmed against an unrelated asset), not from this change; screenshot reviewed.

**Deliberately not done, and why:** US-LIF-04's person half was already Built; this session added only the department half. Allowing an asset to have BOTH a person AND a department custodian simultaneously (the AC says "a person or department" - alternatives, not both; exclusive is the correct reading). A department's own asset-roster view (no AC asks for it; the custodian is recorded on the asset and queryable). Reworking the other 23 optimistic-lock call sites to carry a rich `currentResource` DTO (the handler fix already makes them all correct 409s; the richer body is a separate follow-up).

**Updated status:** US-LIF-04 Partial → **Built**. EPIC-LIF moves from 14 Built / 2 Partial (04, 13) / 0 Not-started to **15 Built / 1 Partial (13 - escalation still can't resolve a "line manager," no people-hierarchy exists) / 0 Not-started**. Overall: **122 Built / 8 Partial / 50 Not started** (180 total), up from 121/9/50. Plus one pre-existing app-wide bug fixed (optimistic-lock conflicts now return 409, not 401).

**Next session:** Partials sweep remainder — LIF-13 (needs a people-management-hierarchy concept, still genuinely blocked), AUD-03 (org-scope design question), SEC-14/USR-08 session-token items, NTF-02 (gateway decision). Or Dependabot triage (18 PRs), or a fresh epic (MIG/SCN/INT). Worth a dedicated follow-up: give optimistic-lock 409s a resource-specific `currentResource` DTO so the asset-edit ConflictDialog can show real server values (the plumbing is now correct; only the snapshot is missing).

## 2026-07-19 — US-USR-08 Partial→Built: a deactivated user's live access token is now revoked at once (stateless-JWT gap closed)

Fourth Partials-sweep item across this run, and the one the last three entries kept naming. US-USR-08's happy-path AC ("status becomes Deactivated, **sessions/refresh tokens revoke**, and the event is logged") was Partial: the asset-blocking check, the refresh-token revocation, and the security-event log were all Built, but a deactivated user's already-issued **stateless JWT access token** stayed valid until its natural expiry (up to 480 min) because the JWT filter trusted the token's claims with no per-request revocation check. `UserDeactivationService`'s own Javadoc named this as "the one part of the AC still not fully closed." Closed now.

**Design: an in-memory revocation registry, seeded at startup, consulted O(1) per request - no DB hit on the auth hot path.** New `AccessRevocationCheck` port in `common.security` (the same port-in-common / adapter-elsewhere pattern as `CurrentUserProvider`), implemented by `DeactivatedUserRegistry` in the `usr` module (which owns the user data). The JWT filter consults it: a structurally-valid, unexpired token whose user is revoked leaves the `SecurityContext` empty exactly as a bad token would, so the existing entry point produces the normal 401 - no new error path. `UserDeactivationService.deactivate()` calls `registry.markDeactivated(userId)` in the same transaction that revokes refresh tokens. Two properties make the in-memory set correct rather than a shortcut: (1) **deactivation is terminal** - `UserStatus` only moves ACTIVE→DEACTIVATED, there is no reactivation flow anywhere in the codebase (verified), so the set only ever grows and never needs an eviction path; (2) the registry **re-seeds from every DEACTIVATED user at startup** (`ApplicationRunner`, `findIdsByStatus`), so the guarantee survives a restart - an access token issued just before a restart is still within its lifetime afterward. Chose this over a per-request DB status lookup precisely because access tokens were made stateless JWTs to avoid a query per request; chose it over a token denylist because revoking by user id is simpler and there are no partial-revocation semantics to model. Known limitation, stated plainly and consistent with every prior epic: the registry is per-instance - this is a single-instance, deployment-local app; a horizontally-scaled deployment would need a shared store (or accept the access-token lifetime as the revocation window).

**Verification:** 3 new backend tests (`DeactivatedUserRegistryTest`: startup-seed from DEACTIVATED users, immediate mark, null-safety) + `UserDeactivationServiceTest` updated (deactivate marks the registry AND revokes refresh tokens; a *blocked* deactivation marks neither - the user stays active). **Full suite: 419/419** (416 + 3). No frontend change: this is an auth-filter change, and a mid-session 401 already routes the SPA to login; the deactivation UI already exists. **Click-tested live 8/8** (native Postgres, backend on 8081): a fresh INVENTORY_MANAGER logs in, its token works (200), admin deactivates it, and **the same still-unexpired token is immediately 401** - the AC. Also proven: the refresh token is revoked (cannot mint a new access token), the user cannot log in again, and **other users are unaffected** (admin's token still 200 - revocation is per-user, not a blanket failure). **Restart-survival proven separately** (the design's whole point): captured a deactivated user's token, restarted the app, watched the registry log "seeded with 5 deactivated user(s)", and confirmed the pre-restart token is STILL 401 after restart while a fresh admin token works - the startup seed does its job across a bounce.

**Deliberately not done, and why:** a shared/distributed revocation store (the single-instance assumption is documented and matches the deployment; premature otherwise); pruning the registry to only users deactivated within one token-lifetime (a bounded-memory optimization, but the set is just UUIDs - not worth the added "when is it safe to forget" logic); a UI toast telling an admin "their sessions were killed" (the security-event log already records USER_DEACTIVATED; no AC asks for the toast).

**Updated status:** US-USR-08 Partial → **Built**. EPIC-USR: one of its Partials closed (US-USR-08). Overall: **123 Built / 7 Partial / 50 Not started** (180 total), up from 122/8/50.

**Next session:** Partials sweep remainder — the genuinely-blocked/decision-needed ones are what's left: LIF-13 (no people-management hierarchy exists), AUD-03 (org-scope design question for category/asset-scoped audits), NTF-02 (SMS gateway decision), SEC-14 (service accounts, a sizable R1 build), CMP-01/ORG-03/USR-04. Or Dependabot triage (18 PRs), or open a fresh untouched epic (MIG/SCN/INT — INT-03 LDAP/SSO is the only R1 Must). The optimistic-lock `currentResource` DTO follow-up (from the previous entry) also still stands.
